Associated Information:
Adolf Hitler, the former German Chancellor, was born on
April 20, 1889, in Braunau am Inn, Austria-Hungary (now
modern-day Austria). He later moved to Germany and
rose to power as the leader of the Nazi Party, becoming
Chancellor in 1933 and dictator of Germany from 1934
to 1945.
12. Which among the following does not fall in
OPEC countries (Malaysia)
Associated Information:
OPEC (Organization of the Petroleum Exporting
Countries) is a cartel of 13 oil-producing countries that
coordinates the production and sale of oil on the global
market. The 13 OPEC countries are: 1. Algeria, 2. Angola,
3. Ecuador (withdrew in 2020, but rejoined in 2022), 4.
Equatorial Guinea, 5. Gabon, 6. Iran, 7. Iraq, 8. Kuwait, 9.
Libya, 10. Nigeria, 11. Qatar, 12. Saudi Arabia, 13. United
Arab Emirates. These countries account for a significant
portion of the world's oil production and exports, and
play a major role in shaping the global oil market.
13. Nelson Mandela of South Africa was released
from prison: (1990)
Associated Information:
Nelson Mandela (1918–2013) was a South African anti-
apartheid activist, politician, and philanthropist whose
life and legacy have left an indelible mark on the world.
He is celebrated for his tireless fight against racial
inequality and his efforts to build a more just and united
South Africa.
Anti-Apartheid Activism: Mandela joined the African
National Congress (ANC) in 1943 and co-founded its
Youth League in 1944. He emerged as a leading figure in
the fight against apartheid, a brutal system of racial
segregation enforced by the South African government.
Initially advocating for nonviolent resistance, Mandela
later became involved in organizing acts of civil
disobedience and other measures to challenge the
oppressive regime. His efforts helped galvanize the anti-
apartheid movement and brought international
attention to South Africa's plight.
Imprisonment: Mandela was arrested in 1962 and spent
27 years in prison, enduring harsh conditions and
isolation. Despite this, he remained a steadfast advocate
for justice and equality, becoming a symbol of resistance
against oppression. His imprisonment became a rallying
point for anti-apartheid activists worldwide, and his
resilience inspired millions.
Presidency and Reconciliation: After his release in 1990,
Mandela led negotiations to end apartheid, culminating
in South Africa's first multiracial elections in 1994, where
he was elected as the country's first black president. As
president, he prioritized national reconciliation,
establishing the Truth and Reconciliation Commission
to address human rights abuses during apartheid.
Mandela's leadership was characterized by his focus on
forgiveness, unity, and nation-building, helping to heal
the deep divisions within South African society.
Legacy and Achievements: Mandela's legacy extends far
beyond his presidency. He is celebrated globally for his
contributions to peace, reconciliation, and social
justice. Some of his notable achievements include:
• Leading South Africa's peaceful transition to
democracy.
• Establishing the Nelson Mandela Foundation,
which focuses on education, rural development,
and HIV/AIDS awareness.
• Advocating for women's rights and gender
equality.
• Receiving over 250 honors and awards, including
the Nobel Peace Prize (1993) and the Presidential
Medal of Freedom from President Barack Obama.
Books by Nelson Mandela
Mandela's writings provide a deep insight into his life
and ideals:
• "Long Walk to Freedom" (1994): His
autobiography, chronicling his journey from rural
South Africa to becoming a global icon.
• "Conversations with Myself" (2010): A collection of
personal reflections, letters, and interviews.
• "Dare Not Linger: The Presidential Years" (2017):
Co-written with Mandla Langa, this book focuses on
Mandela's presidency.
• "The Struggle Is My Life" (1990): A collection of
Mandela's speeches and writings, reflecting his
vision and commitment to justice.

17. Squash Champion World No. 1 professional
squash player one of the greatest in the history
of squash was (Jehangir Khan)
Associated Information:
Jahangir Khan is widely regarded as one of the greatest
squash players in history. A Pakistani professional
squash player, he dominated the sport during the 1980s
and 1990s, achieving unparalleled success. Jahangir won
a record 10 British Open titles and 8 World
Championship titles, solidifying his legacy as a legend in
the sport. From 1981 to 1986, he held the World No. 1
ranking, for five consecutive years and achieved an
incredible unbeaten streak of 555 matches over five
years, one of the longest winning streaks in any
professional sport.
Known for his exceptional skill, speed, and unmatched
endurance, Jahangir was a force to be reckoned with on
the court, earning him the title of the "King of Squash."
His tactical brilliance and dedication to the game set
new benchmarks in professional squash. For his
monumental contributions, he was inducted into the
World Squash Federation Hall of Fame in 1993 and the
Pakistan Sports Hall of Fame in 1994.
Jahangir Khan's impact transcends his numerous titles
and records. He inspired generations of players and

To this day, he is celebrated as a symbol of excellence,
resilience, and unparalleled achievement in the world
of squash

27. Which is the largest swimming course in the
world? (English Channel of UK)
Explanation:
The English Channel is an arm of the Atlantic Ocean that
separates southern England from northern France
Known for its popularity in long-distance swimming, the
channel has hosted numerous record-breaking swims. At
its narrowest point, it is approximately 21 miles (34
kilometers) wide, offering a formidable challenge for
swimmers due to its length, cold water, and strong
currents. While the English Channel is not a "swimming
course in the traditional sense, it is a widely recognized
and celebrated destination for endurance swimmers
worldwide, making it synonymous with long distance
swimming feats.

34. Angiography and Angioplasty are:
(A) Different process
(B) Different but interlinked
(C) One and same
(D) None of above
Associated Information:
Angiography and angioplasty are two separate medical
procedures, but they are often performed together.
Angiography is a diagnostic procedure that uses imaging
techniques to visualize the inside of blood vessels and
organs. Angioplasty, on the other hand, is a therapeutic
procedure that uses a balloon-tipped catheter to widen
narrowed or blocked blood vessels.
While they are different procedures, they are often
performed together to diagnose and treat
cardiovascular diseases. For example, an angiogram may
be performed to diagnose a blockage in an artery, and
then an angioplasty may be performed to open up the
blockage.

79. Usher on irrigated land is: (5%)
Explanation:
The literal meaning of Usher() in Arabic is "ten" or
"one-tenth." It originates from the Arabic word "قرة"
(Asharah), which means ten.
In Islamic taxation, Usher refers to the one-tenth (10%)
tax imposed on agricultural produce obtained from rain-
fed land. However, if the land is irrigated through
artificial means, the usher rate is reduced to one-
twentieth (5%) due to the additional effort and cost
involved in artificial irrigation.
Usher Rates Based on Land Type:
•
Irrigated land )آبپاشی شدہ زمین land watered through.
artificial means like canals or tube wells): 5% Usher is
applicable.
•
Rain-fed land )بارانی زمین( land dependent on natural
rainfall): 10% Usher is applicable

14. Non-permanent members of Security Council
are: (Ten)
Associated Information:
The United Nations Security Council (UNSC) is a powerful
organ of the UN that maintains international peace and
security. It has 15 members, including:
- 5 permanent members with veto power: China, France,
Russia (formerly the Soviet Union), United Kingdom &
United States
- 10 non-permanent members elected for 2-year terms
by the UN General Assembly
Key differences between permanent and non-
permanent members:
Permanent Members:
- Have veto power over UNSC decisions
- May not have to be re-elected
- Do not have to be re-elected
- Have significant influence and leadership roles
Non-Permanent Members:
- Do not have veto power
- Serve for 2-year terms
- Must be re-elected by the UN General Assembly
- Have limited influence compared to permanent
members
Why Permanent Members are there in the Security
Council:
- Historical significance: The 5 permanent members were
the main victors of World War II and were granted
permanent seats in recognition of their role in
establishing the UN.
- Global influence: Permanent members have significant
economic, political, and military influence globally.
- Stability and continuity: Permanent members provide
stability and continuity in the UNSC, ensuring that the
council can respond effectively to global challenges.
- Leadership: Permanent members are expected to take
on leadership roles in maintaining international peace
and security.

31. "Gwadar" is located in: (Makran)
Associated Information:
The name "Gwadar" originates from the Balochi
language, meaning "gateway of winds." Its
strategic location on the Arabian Sea, where favorable
wind patterns facilitate trade and navigation, has earned
it the title of the "Gateway of Winds."
Historical Journey:
Ancient Times: Gwadar served as a key crossroads for
trade between Mesopotamia and the Indus Valley
Civilization.
Arab Conquest (632 AD): It became part of the Umayyad
Caliphate, bolstering trade and communication in the
region.
Muscat Ownership (1783-1861): Oman recognized
Gwadar's coastal value and maintained it as an overseas
possession.
British Era (1861-1947): Administered by the Sultan of
Muscat under British oversight.
Omani Rule (1947-1958): After Pakistan's
independence, Gwadar remained under Omani
administration for 11 years.
Pakistan's Acquisition (1958): Under Prime Minister
Feroz Khan Noon, Pakistan purchased Gwadar from
Oman with significant contributions from Aga-Khan-Nisa

--- Page 5 ---
62 Advanced PPSC MCQs Papers (Volume 2)
Noon and financial support from Aga Khan IV.
Approximately 15,210 sq km (5,870 sq ml) of land was
acquired for 5.5 billion Pakistani rupees (equivalent to
$2 billion USD today).
Official Inauguration (1969): Gwadar port began
handling cargo and trade operations.
China's Lease (2015): Gwadar was leased to China for 40
years under the China-Pakistan Economic Corridor
(CPEC), linking it to China's Belt and Road Initiative (BRI)
and Maritime Silk Road.
China's Interest and Role in Gwadar
1
Strategic Location: Close to the Strait of Hormuz,
Gwadar provides China direct access to the Arabian Sea
and reduces reliance on the Malacca Strait.
Energy Security: Gwadar facilitates secure imports of oll
and gas, strengthening China's energy supply chain.
Economic Growth: Infrastructure development in
Gwadar boosts regional and bilateral economic growth.
Regional Influence: Enhances China's presence in South
Asia and the Middle East.
China's Contributions to Gwadar:
Infrastructure Development: Investments in port
facilities, highways, and energy projects.
Gwadar Port and Free Zone: China operates the port and
free zone, with plans for further expansion.
Regional Connectivity: Gwadar connects to China's
Xinjiang region through CPEC, strengthening trade
routes.
US Interests in Gwadar
Counterbalance to China: Gwadar's strategic location
has drawn US attention as it seeks to counter China's
influence in the region.
Security Concerns: The US has expressed worries about
Gwadar's potential use as a military base by China.
Economic Interests: The US recognizes Gwadar's
potential in trade and the energy sector.
Gwadar's Strategic Importance
1. Location: Situated near the Strait of Hormuz, it
holds immense value for regional trade and energy
routes.
2. Gateway Role: Connects Central Asia, South Asia,
and the Middle East.
3. Trade and Energy: Serves as a critical node for
transshipment and energy security..
4. BRI and CPEC: Integral to China's Belt and Road
Initiative and CPEC, enhancing regional
connectivity.
5. Pakistan's Opportunity: Offers Pakistan economic
growth, infrastructure development, and enhanced
geopolitical influence.

43. Who wrote "Vande Mataram"? (Chandra

Associated Information:
"Vande Mataram" is a Sanskrit phrase that means "I bow
to thee, Mother" or "Hail to the Mother". It is a patriotic
slogan and a hymn dedicated to the Motherland, India.
The phrase was first written by Bankim Chandra
Chattopadhyay, a Bengali poet and novelist, in his novel
"Anandamath" In 1882. It was later popularized by
Rabindranath Tagore, a Nobel laureate and a close friend
of Mahatma Gandhi.

50. Greenland & Antarctica contains of world total
ice: (99%)
Associated Information:
Greenland and Antarctica: The World's Ice Reservoirs
Greenland and Antarctica are the two largest ice bodies
on Earth, collectively containing about 99% of the
planet's ice. These regions are critical to regulating
global climate, sea levels, and weather patterns.
Greenland
Location: North Atlantic, northeast of Canada and
northwest of Europe.
Size: Approximately 2.175 million km² (843,000 sq mi).
Ice Coverage: About 80% of Greenland is covered in ice,
with an average thickness of 1.5-2 km (0.9-1.2 mi).
Ice Volume: Approximately 2.5 million km³ (1 million cu
mi).
Impact: Greenland's melting ice contributes significantly
to sea level rise, adding 0.7-1.1 mm (0.03-0.04 in)
annually.
Antarctica
Location: Southern Hemisphere, surrounding the South
Pole.
Size: Approximately 14 million km² (5.4 million sq mi).


--- Page 63 ---
Ice Coverage: About 98% of Antarctica is covered in Ice,
with an average thickness of 2-3 km (1.2-1.9 mi).
Ice Volume: Approximately 30 million km³ (7.2 million
cu mi).
Impact: Antarctica's vast ice sheet plays a key role in
regulating global sea levels, with its potential melting
capable of raising sea levels by 3-4 meters (10-13 ft).
Comparison
Size and Volume: Antarctica Is 6-7 times larger than
Greenland and contains about 91% of Earth's ice,
compared to Greenland's 8%.
Melting Susceptibility:
Greenland's ice is more prone to melting due to lower
elevation and proximity to warmer ocean currents.
•
Antarctica's ice is more stable but still vulnerable
to climate change and warming ocean currents.
Importance
Both Greenland and Antarctica are critical to:
1. Climate Regulation: Their ice sheets influence
global temperatures and weather patterns.
2. Sea Levels: Changes in ice volume directly affect
coastal communities worldwide.
3. Ocean Currents: Ice melt impacts salinity and
circulation, altering global ocean currents.
Key Statistic
Greenland and Antarctica together hold 99% of the
Earth's ice, with Antarctica accounting for 91% and
Greenland 8%. Their collective role in maintaining
Earth's climate and sea levels makes them vital to the
planet's environmental stability.
51. Which is called "Roof of the World"? (Tibet)
Associated Information:
The Tibetan Plateau, often referred to as the "Roof of
the World", is the world's highest and largest plateau.
Located in the Himalayan region, it boasts an average
elevation of over 4,500 meters (14,764 feet) above sea
level. This extraordinary altitude makes it one of the
most remarkable geographical features on Earth, serving
as home to some of the world's most stunning natural
wonders and iconic mountain peaks..
Key Features of the Tibetan Plateau:
1.
Highest Peaks: The Tibetan Plateau is home to
several of the world's highest mountains, including:
Ο
2.
Mount Everest: The highest mountain on Earth at
8,848 meters (29,029 feet).
K2, Kangchenjunga, and Annapurna: Other
towering peaks located along the Himalayan range.
Countries Spanning the Plateau: The Tibetan
Plateau covers parts of five countries, making it a
geopolitically significant region:
。
China: Includes the Tibet Autonomous Region,
Qinghai, Xinjiang, Gansu, Yunnan, and Sichuan
provinces.
India: Includes parts of Jammu and Kashmir,
Himachal Pradesh, Uttarakhand, Sikkim, and
Arunachal Pradesh.
Nepal: Shares the plateau's southern edge, along
with parts of the Himalayan range.
Bhutan: Located on the southeastern fringe of the
plateau.
Ο
Papers of 2019
63
Pakistan: Includes portions of Gilgit-Baltistan in the
Karakoram range.
3. Significance:
Ο
Ο
Natural Wonders: The Tibetan Plateau is home to
breathtaking landscapes, including high-altitude
deserts, glaciers, and pristine lakes.
Climate Regulation: Often referred to as the "Third
Pole", the plateau plays a crucial role in regulating
the Earth's climate and serves as the source of
many major rivers.
Cultural Importance: It is central to Tibetan culture,
Buddhism, and spirituality, with its monasteries and
traditions holding global significance.
52. "Lake Baikal" is in: (Siberia)
Associated Information:
Lake Baikal is located in southern Siberia, Russia, and is
renowned as one of the world's most extraordinary
natural wonders. It is both the deepest and largest
freshwater lake by volume, holding approximately 20%
of the world's unfrozen freshwater.
Key Facts About Lake Baikal:
Deepest Lake in the World: Reaches a depth of
approximately 5,387 feet (1,642 meters).
Largest Freshwater Lake by Volume: Contains about
23,615 cubic kilometers (5,662 cubic miles) of
freshwater, which is more than all the North American
Great Lakes combined.
Oldest Lake: Estimated to be around 25 million years
old, making it the oldest lake in the world.
Unique Biodiversity: Home to over 2,500 species of
plants and animals, with many being endemic (found
nowhere else). Notable species include the Baikal seal
(nerpa), the only freshwater seal in the world.
Cultural and Natural Significance: Designated as a
UNESCO World Heritage Site in 1996 due to its unique
ecosystem and geological importance.

66. Complete the series: 1,2,5,12,27,58......? (121)
Solution:
1, 2, 5, 12, 27, 58, 121
1x2+0=2
2x2+1=5
5x2+2=12
12 x 2 + 13 = 27
27 x 2 + 4 = 58
58x2+5= 121
67. 12.5% is Equal to which fraction? (1/8)
Explanation:
12.5% can be converted to a fraction by dividing by
100:
12.5 100 0.125
This can be written as a fraction:
0.125 = 1/8
So, 12.5% is equal to 1/8.
68. The ratio of 3.5 kg to 280 gm is? (25:2)
Solution:
To find the ratio, we need to convert both weights
to the same unit. Let's convert 280 gm to kg:
280 gm = 0.28 kg (since 1 kg = 1000 gm)
Now, we can find the ratio:
3.5 kg: 0.28 kg = 3.5/0.28 = 12.5
To simplify the ratio, we can multiply both numbers
by 2:
12.5x2: 1× 2 = 25:2

--- Page 65 ---
So, the correct answer is: (C) 25:2

Associated Information:
Ibn Jarir al-Tabari (838-923 CE) was a renowned Persian
scholar and historian who wrote extensively on Islamic
theology, jurisprudence, and history. His most famous
work is the book "Jami' al-Bayan 'an Tawil al-Quran" (The
Comprehensive Collection on the Interpretation of the
Verses of the Quran), also known as "Tafsir al-Tabari".
However, Al-Tibri is also known for his book on Hadiths,
"Al-Tibri's Collection of Hadiths", which is considered an
important collection of prophetic traditions in Islam.

2. What is the approximate length of the Great
Wall of China? (21196.18km)
Associated Information:
The Great Wall of China is approximately 21,196.18 km
(13,170.7 miles) long, with slight variations in length
depending on measurement methods and sources. This
iconic structure is not a single wall but a series of
separate walls built by cross different dynasties, starting in
the 7th century BC. Its most well-known sections were
constructed during the Ming Dynasty (1368-1644) and
span about 8,851.8 km (5,500 miles).

23. "Hayat-e-Jawaid" written by Altaf Hussain Hali
is on the life of: (Sir Syed Ahmad Khan)
Associated Information:
"Hayat-e-Jawaid" حیات جاوید is a biography written by
Altaf Hussain Hali in 1888. The book is a comprehensive
account of the life and times of Sir Syed Ahmad Khan
(1817-1898),
prominent Muslim reformer,
educationist, and founder of the Aligarh Muslim
University.
a
The biography provides valuable insights into Sir Syed's
life, his contributions to the Muslim community, and his
efforts to promote education and social reform. Hali's
work is considered a significant contribution to Urdu
literature and a vital source of information on Sir Syed's
life and legacy.

24. Quaid-i-Azam Muhammad Ali Jinnah

25. Mirani Dam is located in which province?
(Baluchistan)
26. The Muslim demand for Separate Electorate
presented by the Shimla Deputation 1906 was
incorporated in the: (Minto Morley Reforms)
Associated Information:
The Muslim demand for a Separate Electorate,
presented by the Shimla Deputation in 1906, was
incorporated in the Minto-Morley Reforms. The Shimla
Deputation consisted of 35 prominent Muslim leaders
who met with Lord Minto, the Viceroy of India, to
articulate their political demands, emphasizing the need
for separate electorates to safeguard Muslim politicai
representation. This demand was accepted and
formalized through the Indian Councils Act of 1909,
commonly referred to as the Minto-Morley Reforms. It
marked a turning point in Indian political history,
introducing separate electorates for Muslims and
recognizing their distinct political identity. This
development laid the groundwork for future
constitutional debates and highlighted growing
communal divisions during the British colonial era.

Currently, Former senator JD Vance (James David Vance)
of Ohio is the 50th Vice President the United States. He
was selected by President-elect Donald Trump as his

presidential election on November 5. Their

Vance, born on August 2, 1984, in Middletown, Ohio, is
a U.S. Senator, venture capitalist, and author. He gained
national prominence with his bestselling memoir,
Hillbilly Elegy, which explores the challenges faced by
working-class families In America. After a successful
career in venture capital, Vance entered politics and was
elected to the U.S. Senate in 2022. Known for his
advocacy for conservative policies and focus on
economic reform, he has emerged as a key ally of
President Trump. He succeeded Kamala Harris, who
served alongside President Joe Biden since 2021.

Geography
42. Which of the following found in US? (Mount
McKinley, Death Valley, Appalachians, All of
these)
Associated Information:
- Mount McKinley (now officially known as Denali) is
located in Alaska, USA. It's the highest peak in North
America.
- Death Valley is a desert valley located in Eastern
California, USA. It's known for being one of the hottest
and driest places on Earth.
- The Appalachian Mountains are a range of mountains
that stretch from Quebec, Canada, to Alabama, USA. A
significant portion of the Appalachians is located in the
Eastern United States.

44. Clark Glacier is located in? (USA)
45. Trout Lake is situated in: (USA)
Explanation:
Trout Lake is a name shared by various bodies of water
and communities across multiple countries. Here's an
overview:
United States:
Washington: Trout Lake is a census-designated place
known for its outdoor recreational activities.
Michigan: An unincorporated community and township
named Trout Lake are located in the Upper Peninsula.
Colorado: Trout Lake near Telluride is a scenic spot
popular for fishing and hiking.
New York: Several lakes named Trout Lake are found in
Hamilton and Warren counties.
Wisconsin: Trout Lake in Vilas County is renowned for its
clear waters and fishing opportunities.
Canada:
Ontario: Trout Lake borders the city of North Bay and is
a popular destination for water activities.
British Columbia: A rural community and lake named
Trout Lake are situated in the West Kootenay region.
Alberta: An unincorporated community named Trout
Lake is located in the province.
Northwest Territories: Sambaa K'e, formerly known as
Trout Lake, is both a lake and a community in this region.
Other Countries:
South Africa: In the Eastern Cape, there's a location
known as Trout Lake, celebrated for its natural beauty.
This Illustrates that "Trout Lake" is a common name for
various lakes and communities, predominantly in the
United States and Canada, with notable instances in
South Africa.

Everyday Science
46. Which of the following elements comes first in
Periodic Table? (Hydrogen)
47. Which of the following colours are primary
colours? (Red, Blue, Green)
48. In human which body part develop first? (Heart)
Associated Information:
Fertilization: When the sperm successfully waltzes into
the egg, fertilization occurs. The resulting zygote
contains a full complement of genetic material,
combining both parental contributions.
Embryonic Development: The zygote then goes through
several stages: morula, blastula, gastrula, and neurula.
These fancy names represent critical milestones in
shaping our future selves.
Implantation: Around a week after fertilization, the
embryo hatches from its protective protein shell (the
zona pellucida) and snuggles up against the uterine
lining. It's like finding the perfect spot at a cozy party!
Organ Formation: The heart leads the way, developing
first around 3-4 weeks, followed by other like:
- Brain: 3-4 weeks
- Lungs: 4-5 weeks
- Kidneys: 5-6 weeks
Grand Finale: By the end of this miraculous process, our
lungs-the ultimate oxygen exchange hubs-complete
their development.
The heart starts beating around 6 weeks after
fertilization.

58. Who co-founded Hotmail in 1996 and then
sold it to Microsoft? (Sabeer Bhatia)
Associated Information:
Hotmail was founded in 1996 by Sabeer Bhatia and Jack
Smith. In 1997, Microsoft acquired it for an estimated
$400 million, rebranding it as MSN Hotmail. Later, it
became part of the Windows Live suite as Windows Live
Hotmail. Microsoft phased out Hotmail in October 2011,
relaunching the service as Outlook.com in 2012.

64. What is the area of a triangle having base 19m
and height 7m? (66.5 m²)
Solution:
Base = 19 m, height = 7m
Area of triangle
= 1/2 (Base x height)
= 1/2 (19 x 7)
= 133/2
= 66.5
65. 2 ÷ 0.5 = ? (4)
Solution:
2 ÷ 0.5
= 2 ÷ 5/10
= 2 ÷ 1/2
= 2 x 2/1
= 4
66. Complete the series 1, 8, 4, 27, 9,
(64)
Solution:
1, 8, 4, 27, 9, 64
1² = 1, 2³ = 8, 3² = 9, 4³ = 64
2² = 4, 3³ = 27, 4² = 16
67. 2 + (-2) = ? (0)
Solution:
= 2 + (-2)
= 2 - 2 = 0
68. Complete the series: 36, 34, 30, 28, 24,
(22)
Solution:
36, 34, 30, 28, 24, 22
-2 -4 -2 -4 -2
36 - 2 = 34, 34 - 4 = 30
30 - 2 = 28, 28 - 4 = 24
24 - 2 = 22, 22 - 4 = 18
69. When 20% of itself added into a number it gives
102, find the number. (85)
Solution:
Let the number be x
x + 20/100 x = 102
x + 0.2x = 102
1.2 x = 102
x = 102/1.2
x = 85
70. 30% of 100 is equal to 3% of
(1000)
Solution:
30/100 × 100 = 3/100 × x
30 = 3/100 x
30 x 100/3 = x
1000 = x

PAPER 10 Assistant (BS-16)
(2019) Labour & Human

General Knowledge
1. Which is the capital city of Canada? (Ottawa)
2. Julius Caesar was a politician and general of
(Italy)
Associated Information:
Julius Caesar (100-44 BCE) was a Roman general and
statesman whose influence shaped the course of Roman
and world history. Key highlights of his life include:
Political Rise: Rose to prominence in the 1st century BCE
and formed the First Triumvirate with Pompey and
Crassus.
Civil War: His crossing of the Rubicon River with his
legions initiated a civil war, fundamentally altering the
Roman Republic.
Reforms: Introduced significant reforms, including the
Julian calendar, which influenced the modern calendar
system.
منشی نول کشور ناول نویس نہیں تھے۔ ان کا میدان صحافت، طباعت، اور علمی و ادبی کتابوں کی
اشاعت تھا۔ اگرچہ ان کے پریس سے کئی ادبی اور تاریخی کتابیں شائع ہوئی ہیں لیکن انہوں نے
خود بھی ناول تحریر نہیں کیا۔ ان کی خدمات کا بنیادی محور اردو زبان، ادب، اور صحافت کی
ترقی تھا، ناول نویسی نہیں ۔
(C) طباعت قرآن پاک (Printing of the Quran)
اگرچہ منشی نول کشور کے پریس نے قرآن پاک کی طباعت کی اور یہ ان کا ایک اہم کارنامہ تھا،
لیکن ان کی سب سے بڑی اور نمایاں خدمات صحافت اور اخبار نویسی کے میدان میں تھیں۔
ان کے جاری کردہ اور وہ اخبار نے اردو صحافت میں انقلاب برپا کیا، جو ان کی پہچان ہی۔
طباعت قرآن پاک ان کی خدمات کا ایک حصہ ضرور تھا، لیکن ان کی بنیادی شناخت اخبار
نویسی رہی۔
(D) ادبی تاریخ نویسی (Literary Historiography)
منشی نول کشور نے براہ راست ادبی تاریخ نویسی نہیں کی۔ ان کے پریس نے بہت سی ادبی اور
تاریخی کتابیں شائع کیں، جن میں داستانیں، شاعری، اور دیگر ادبی موضوعات شامل تھے۔
لیکن انہوں نے خود ادبی تاریخ نہیں لکھی۔ ان کا کام اردو ادب کے ذخائر کو محفوظ کرنے اور
عام کرنے کا تھا، جو ان کی اشاعتی خدمات کے ذریعے ممکن ہوا۔
صحیح جواب (B) اخبار نویسی کیوں؟
منشی نول کشور کا سب سے بڑا کارنامہ اور اخبار کا اجرا تھا، جو اردو صحافت کا ایک سنگ میل
ثابت ہوا۔ 26 نومبر 1858 میں انھوں نے اودھ اخبار کا اجرا کیا جو بڑے سائز کے چار
صفحات پر مبنی ہوتا تھا۔ اس اخبار نے اردو زبان کو فروغ دیا، عوام کو باخبر رکھا، اور صحافت میں
معیار قائم کیا۔ ان کی یہی خدمات انہیں اردو صحافت کے میدان میں ممتاز کرتی ہیں اور اس
سوال کا درست جواب "اخبار نویسی" ہے۔
یہ تفصیل واضح کرتی ہے کہ دیگر آپشنز کیوں درست نہیں ہیں اور منشی نول کشور کی بنیادی
خدمات کس میدان میں تھیں

3. In which city the first WHO Global Conference

4. As a part of the Treaty of Versailles that ended
World War I the ILO was created in: (1919)
Associated Information:
The Treaty of Versailles, signed on June 28, 1919, was a
peace settlement that officially ended World War I. It
addressed multiple aspects of post-war recovery and
reorganization, with the creation of the International
Labour Organization (ILO) as one of its key
achievements.
Key Aims of the Treaty:
1. End of War: Officially concluded the state of war
between Germany and the Allied Powers (France,
Britain, the U.S., etc.).
2. Imposition of Penalties: Placed significant
economic and territorial penalties on Germany.
3. Border Adjustments: Redrew international
borders, leading to territorial losses for Germany.
4. Creation of the League of Nations: Aimed to
promote global peace and prevent future conflicts.
Major Provisions of the Treaty:
1. War Guilt Clause: Germany accepted full
responsibility for the war.
2. Reparations: Germany was obligated to pay
reparations to the Allies.
3. Territorial Adjustments: Loss of territories such as
Alsace-Lorraine, Saar Basin, and colonies.
4. Military Restrictions: Germany's military
capabilities were heavily curtailed.
5. Creation of the ILO: Established to improve labor
conditions, promote rights, and enhance economic
justice globally.
Consequences of the Treaty:
1. Resentment in Germany: Harsh terms fueled
nationalist resentment, setting the stage for the rise
of Nazi Germany.
2. World War II: The treaty's failures and Germany's
rearmament contributed to the outbreak of World
War II.
3. Territorial Redrawing: Led to the creation of new
states like Poland and Czechoslovakia.
Legacy of the Treaty:
Critics: Argued it was excessively punitive, fostering
future conflict.
Supporters: Believed it was necessary to prevent future
aggression.
International Cooperation: Marked the beginning of
modern collective security efforts through the League of
Nations and the ILO.
The International Labour Organization (ILO), created in
1919, remains one of the lasting achievements of the
treaty, focusing on promoting social justice, labor rights,
and fair working conditions worldwide.

6. International organization "Human Rights
Watch" is based in: (New York)
Associated Information:
Human Rights Watch (HRW) is an internationally
renowned non-governmental organization dedicated to
the protection and promotion of human rights
worldwide. Founded in 1978 by Robert L. Bernstein and
Aryeh Neier, HRW is headquartered in New York City,
with a presence in over 90 countries through regional
offices and affiliates.
Mission and Objectives:
HRW works to safeguard the principles of justice, dignity,
and equality. Its primary mission is to:
• Investigate and document human rights violations.
• Expose abuses to the global community through
reports and media.
• Advocate for policy changes and accountability for
violators.
• Support activists, victims, and marginalized
communities.
Key Focus Areas:
Conflict Zones: Addressing human rights abuses in war
and crisis-affected areas.
Refugee and Migrant Rights: Advocating for the
protection and fair treatment of displaced individuals.
Women's Rights and Gender Equality: Campaigning for
the eradication of violence and discrimination against
women.
LGBTQ+ Rights: Promoting inclusivity and protections
for LGBTQ+ individuals.
Racial Justice and Equality: Combating systemic racism
and discrimination.
Economic, Social, and Cultural Rights: Ensuring access to
education, healthcare, and economic equity.
Environmental and Human Rights: Addressing the
intersection of ecological harm and human rights.
International Justice: Supporting mechanisms for
accountability, including tribunals and sanctions.
Impact:
HRW's rigorous investigations and advocacy have led to
tangible policy changes and greater accountability for
human rights abuses. The organization's global reach
and dedication to justice make it a cornerstone of
modern human rights advocacy.

Associated Information/Updates about the EU:
As of January 2026, the European Union (EU) comprises.
27 member states.
Capital: Brussels, Belgium.
Population: Over 450 million people.
Official Languages: 24.
Euro Currency: Adopted by 21 member states.
Founding: Established as the European Economic
Community (EEC) in 1958; became the European Union
in 1993.
Economy: One of the largest globally, with a Gross
Domestic Product (GDP) exceeding $18 trillion.
Area: Approximately 4,236,351 square kilometers.
Geographical Features: Longest River: Danube,
spanning about 2,860 kilometers. Highest Mountain:
Mont Blanc, at 4,808 meters. Lowest Point: Lago di
Garda, at -65 meters.
Key Objectives and Achievements of the EU:
Economic Integration: Established a single market and
customs union to facilitate free movement of goods,
services, capital, and people.
Political Cooperation: Aims to foster political unity and
collaborative decision-making among member states.
Peace and Stability: Committed to promoting peace and
stability across Europe.
Human Rights: Advocates for human rights and
individual freedoms.
Economic Growth: Supports sustainable economic
growth and development.
Current Challenges Facing the EU:
Migration: Managing migration flows and integrating
migrants.
Climate Change: Addressing environmental concerns
and implementing green policies.
Economic Disparities: Balancing economic growth
across diverse member states.
Political Unity: Maintaining cohesion amid differing
national interests.
Post-Brexit Relations: Navigating the implications of the
United Kingdom's departure from the EU.
The EU continues to evolve, striving to meet these
challenges while upholding its foundational principles of
unity, cooperation, and prosperity.

35. "Rabi" season begins in: (October-December)
Associated Information:
In Pakistan, the agricultural cycle is primarily divided into
Rabi and Kharif seasons, along with transitional periods.
Here's how these seasons function in the context of
Pakistan:
1., Rabi Season (October-December):
Start: Sowing begins in October to December, marking
the onset of the winter cropping season.
Harvesting: Takes place in April to May, at the end of
winter and start of spring.
Key Crops in Pakistan: Wheat (the staple crop), barley,
gram, mustard, and lentils.


--- Page 73 ---
Papers of 2019
73
Irrigation: The season relies heavily on irrigation from
rivers and dams (e.g., Tarbela and Mangla), as rainfall is
minimal during this period.
Climatic Requirements: Cool weather during sowing and
moderately warm weather during the harvesting phase.
2. Kharif Season (April-June):
Start: Sowing begins with the onset of the summer
season in April to June.
Harvesting: Occurs from October to November.
Key Crops in Pakistan: Rice, sugarcane, maize, millet,
cotton, and pulses.
Irrigation Dependency: Kharif crops depend on
monsoon rains and canal irrigation systems.
Climatic Challenges: Delayed or erratic monsoons can
severely impact Kharif yields.
3. Zaid Season (March-May):
Duration: A short transitional season between Rabi and
Kharif, spanning March to May.
Key Crops in Pakistan: Seasonal fruits (watermelon,
muskmelon) and vegetables.
Significance: Serves as a bridge season with a smaller
crop output compared to Rabi and Kharif.

39. The Lucknow Pact granted the right of separate
electorates to the: (Muslims)
Associated Information:
The Lucknow Pact was a landmark political agreement
signed on December 29, 1916, between the Indian
National Congress (INC) and the All-India Muslim
League (AIML). It marked an important effort to present
a united front against British colonial rule while
addressing key concerns of both Hindus and Muslims.
Key Aspects of the Lucknow Pact:
1. Electoral Representation: A system of joint
electorates was proposed, allowing Hindus and
Muslims to vote together for representatives in
certain constituencies.
2. Separate Electorates for Muslims: The pact
granted Muslims the right to separate electorates,
meaning they could vote exclusively for their
representatives. This provision ensured that
Muslims would have guaranteed political
representation proportionate to their population.
3. Weightage for Muslim Representation: In
provinces where Muslims were a minority, the pact
provided weightage (extra representation) to
ensure they had a stronger voice in governance.
4. Hindu-Muslim Unity: The pact was designed to
foster cooperation between Hindus and Muslims,
a necessary step for presenting a united opposition
to British rule.
Significance of the Lucknow Pact:
1. First Major Agreement: The Lucknow Pact was the
first significant agreement between the INC and
AIML, reflecting their shared goals.
2. Unity in the Freedom Struggle: It promoted Hindu-
Muslim unity, a key element in the fight for indian
self-rule.
3. Influence on Future Politics: The pact laid the
groundwork for future political negotiations and
ultimately influenced the two-nation theory and
the creation of Pakistan.
Limitations and Criticisms:
1. Limited Scope: The pact focused primarily on
representation in the Imperial Legislative Council,
neglecting broader social or economic reforms.
2. Incomplete Unity: While it aimed for Hindu-Muslim
unity, the pact did not fully resolve religious and
political divides, which persisted and widened over
time.
Historical Context and Legacy:
The Lucknow Pact remains a significant milestone in
Indian history, symbolizing the first major attempt at
collaboration between two key political groups.
Although its success in fostering long-term Hindu-
Muslim unity was limited, it highlighted the importance
of addressing minority concerns and set a precedent for

--- Page 74 ---
74
Advanced PPSC MCQs Papers (Volume 2)
political agreements In India's struggle for
independence.

43. According to the Indus Water Treaty Pakistan
obtained exclusive rights for the three western
rivers which included: (Indus, Jhelum and
Chenab)
Associated Information:
The Indus Water Treaty (IWT) is a landmark agreement
between India and Pakistan, signed on September 19,
1960, in Karachi. It was mediated by the World Bank and
is regarded as one of the most successful water-sharing
agreements globally.
Mediators of the Treaty:
1. Eugene Black: Then-President of the World Bank,
instrumental in facilitating negotiations.
2. Iliff Pike: Canadian engineer and water resources
expert who assisted in drafting the treaty.
3. Michel G. Venne: French engineer and water
resources expert, representing the World Bank in
negotiations.
Key Aspects of the Indus Water Treaty:
1. Water Sharing:
Ο
India was granted control over the eastern rivers
(Ravi, Beas, and Sutlej).
Pakistan was granted control over the western
rivers (Indus, Jhelum, and Chenab).
2. Indus Basin:
Defines the Indus River system and its tributarles as
the primary source of water allocation between the
two countries.
3. Water Usage:
The treaty permits water use for agricultural,
domestic, and industrial purposes.
Prohibits water usage for navigation or storage
without explicit agreement.
4. Dispute Resolution Mechanism:
Ο
Establishes a framework to address disputes
and disagreements over water usage and
treaty violations.
5. Inspections and Data Exchange:
Ο Mandates regular inspections and data sharing
between India and Pakistan to ensure compliance
and transparency.
Significance of the Treaty:
1. Peaceful Coexistence:
2.
3.
0
Despite ongoing political tensions, the treaty has
helped maintain peaceful water-sharing relations
between India and Pakistan.
Water Security:
Guarantees water supply for agriculture, industry,
and domestic needs, especially for Pakistan, whose
economy heavily depends on the Indus River
system.
Economic Benefits:
Facilitates economic growth by enabling irrigation
projects, hydroelectric power generation, and
other water-dependent infrastructure.
Challenges and Controversies:
1. Interpretation Disputes:
2.
India and Pakistan often differ in their
interpretations of certain provisions of the treaty,
causing periodic disagreements.
Water Scarcity:
Climate change, population growth, and increased
water demand have strained the treaty's allocation
framework.
3. Hydroelectric Projects in Disputed Regions:
Ο
Ο
Pakistan has raised concerns over India's illegle
construction of hydroelectric projects in Occupied
Jammu and Kashmir, which is a violation of the
treaty's terms.
These projects threaten water flow into Pakistan
and raise fears of strategic manipulation of water
resources.

48. Which country has its land mass in two
continents? (Türkiye)
Associated Information:
Countries with landmasses spanning two continents are
geographically significant due to their transcontinental
nature. Here is a detailed list:
1. Russia (Europe and Asia): The largest
transcontinental country, spanning the vast expanse of
Eastern Europe and northern Asia. The Ural Mountains
serve as the natural boundary between Europe and Asia.
2. Türkiye (Europe and Asia): Straddles southeastern
Europe and western Asia, divided by the Bosporus
Strait, the Sea of Marmara, and the Dardanelles. Major
cities like Istanbul are transcontinental.
3. Azerbaijan (Europe and Asia): Located at the
crossroads of Eastern Europe and Western Asia, with
the Caucasus Mountains marking the continental
boundary. The country lies primarily in Asia but has a
small portion in Europe.

--- Page 75 ---
16
4. Georgia (Europe and Asia): Positioned at the
intersection of Eastern Europe and Western Asia, with
the Caucasus Mountains forming the division. Its
cultural and political affiliations often align with Europe.
5. Kazakhstan (Europe and Asia): The largest landlocked
country in the world, situated mostly in Asla but with a.
portion, west of the Ural River, considered part of
Europe.
6. Egypt (Africa and Asia): Primarily in North Africa, but
the Sinai Peninsula extends into Asia, making it a
transcontinental nation. The Suez Canal serves as the
dividing line.
7. Israel (Asia and Africa): Geographically part of Asia,
but sometimes considered connected to Africa through
the Sinai Peninsula (political affiliations and historical
ties also factor in).
8. Jordan (Asia and Africa): Primarily an Asian country,
but the Gulf of Aqaba provides a geographical link to
Africa, particularly through its proximity to Egypt's Sinai.
9. Cyprus (Europe and Asia): Geographically located in
Western Asia, but politically and culturally affiliated with
Europe. Its location in the Eastern Mediterranean
connects it to both continents.
10. Greece (Europe and Asia): While mainland Greece is
entirely in Europe, some interpretations suggest that the
island of Crete geographically and historically links it to
Asia due to ancient trade routes and cultural ties.

55. A nerve cell is called: (Neuron)
Associated Information:
The human body is made up of a diverse array of cells,
each specialized to perform distinct functions. Here is a
detailed overview of key cell types in the human body:
Types of Cells in the Human Body:
1. Epithelial Cells:
Form the lining of organs, glands, and external body
surfaces.
Examples include squamous cells (outer skin layer),
cuboidal cells (lining of glands), and columnar cells
(lining of the digestive tract).
2. Connective Tissue Cells:
Ο
0
Bone cells (osteocytes): Support and structure the
skeleton.
Cartilage cells (chondrocytes): Provide flexible
support in joints.
Fat cells (adipocytes): Store energy and provide
insulation.
0
Papers of 2019
75
Blood cells: Include red blood cells, white blood
cells, and platelets.
3. Muscle Cells:
0
Ο
Skeletal muscle cells (fibers): Responsible for
voluntary movement.
Smooth muscle cells: Found in internal organs and
blood vessels.
Cardiac muscle cells: Control the beating of the
heart.
4. Nerve Cells (Neurons):
Ο
Ο
Specialized to transmit and process information.
Neurons are the longest cells in the human body,
with some reaching lengths of up to 1 meter (3.3
feet).
They consist of a cell body, dendrites (receive
signals), and an axon (transmits signals).
5. Blood Cells:
Ο
Ο
Ο
Red Blood Cells (RBCs): Transport oxygen
throughout the body.
White Blood Cells (WBCs): Defend against
infections.
Platelets: Facilitate blood clotting to prevent
bleeding.
6. Stem Cells:
Ο
Undifferentiated cells capable of developing into
various specialized cell types.
Found in bone marrow and other tissues.
7. Immune Cells:
Ο
T cells: Orchestrate immune responses.
B cells: Produce antibodies to fight infections.
Macrophages: Engulf and destroy foreign particles..
8. Endocrine Cells:
Ο
Produce hormones that regulate bodily functions
such as growth, metabolism, and reproduction.
9. Intestinal Cells:
Absorptive cells: Specialized for nutrient
absorption.
Goblet cells: Produce mucus to lubricate the
digestive tract.
10. Reproductive Cells:
Ο
The Ovum (egg cell): The largest cell in the human
body, with a diameter of 0.1-0.2 mm. This haploid
cell contains genetic material and can be fertilized
by a sperm cell.
Key Facts:
•
Largest Cell: The ovum (egg cell),
•
Longest Cell: The nerve cell (neuron), which can
extend up to 1 meter in length.
There are over 200 distinct cell types in the human
body, each critical to maintaining life and
functionality.
56. Which two organs are mainly affected by
malaria? (Spleen and liver)
Associated Information:
Malaria is a mosquito-borne disease caused by the
Plasmodium parasite. The two organs mainly affected by
malaria are:
1. Spleen: The spleen becomes enlarged and congested
with infected red blood cells, leading to splenomegaly.

--- Page 76 ---
76
Advanced PPSC MCQs Papers (Volume 2)
The spleen's filtering function is impaired, causing
anemia, fatigue, and other complications.
2. Liver: The liver becomes congested with infected red
blood cells, leading to hepatomegaly. The liver's
detoxification functions are impaired, causing Jaundice,
and the liver may become damaged.
While other organs like the kidneys, lungs, heart, and
brain can also be affected in severe cases of malaria, the
spleen and liver are the primary organs impacted.

Basic Mathematics
66. (5/6) x (2/5) = ? (1/3)
Solution:
5/6 x 2/5
= 10/30
= 1/3
67. A table listed at Rs. 160 is marked 20% off.
What is the sale price? (Rs. 128)
Solution:
Table price = 160
20% of off = (20/100) x 160
= 32
S.P = 160 - 32 = 128
68. A train moves past a telegraph post and a
bridge 264 m long in 8 seconds and 20 seconds
respectively. What is the speed of the train? (79
km/hr)
Solution:
Length of bridge = 264 m
Time taken to pass the bridge = 20s
Time taken to pass the port = 8s
Suppose length of the train = x m
Speed = Distance/Time
x/8 = (264 + x)/20
20x = 264 x 8 + 8x
20x - 8x = 2112
12x = 2112
x = 2112/12
x = 176
Speed of the train
= 176/8 = 22 m/s
= 22 x (18/5)
= 79.2 km/h
69. A toy is sold for Rs. 220. What was the cost, if
the rate of profit was 10% of the cost? (Rs. 200)
Solution:
S.P = 220
Let C.P = x
S.P = C.P + Profit %
220 = x + 10% of x
220 = x + (10/100)x
220 = 1.1x
x = 220/1.1
x = 200
70. How many tiles of dimension 10 square inch are
required to cover a floor of dimension of 5 feet
by 4 feet? (288)
Solution:
200 = x (This seems like a typo, should be part of the calculation)
1 feet = 12 inches
Dimension of floor = 5 feet x 4 feet
= 5 x 12 + 4 x 12 (This should be 5x12 * 4x12 for area, or (5x12) by (4x12) for dimensions)
= 60 x 48
= 2880 square inches
Dimension of tile = 10 inch²
Total tiles = 2880/10 = 288
71. A milkman adds 10 litre water in 10 litre milk.
His son takes 15 litre of the milk and adds 5 litre
water in it. Find out the amount of water in litres
in this milk? (12.5)
Solution:
Mixture of milk and water
= 10l + 10 liters
= 20 liters
⇒ So, milk water ratio is 1:1
⇒ Son takes 15 liters of mixture i.e. 7.5 liter milk
+7.5 liter water
⇒ Water = 7.5 liter
⇒ After adding 5 liter of water = 7.5 + 5
Total water = 12.5 liter

77
Solution:
(-3)³ = (-3) (-3) (-3)
= (9) (-3)
= -27

83. سودیشی ریل کس کا مزاحیہ مضمون ہے؟ (شوکت تھانوی)
84. مولانا ظفر علی خاں کہاں کے تعلیم یافتہ تھے ؟ (علی گڑھ کالج)
85. ٹک ٹک ، چھم چھم ، ریں ریں، دھک دھنگ وغیرہ الفاظ قواعد کی
رو سے ہیں: (اسم صوت)
اردو گرامر میں اسم کی اقسام:
اردو گرامر میں اسم (Noun) کی مختلف اقسام کو تفصیل سے بیان کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ یہ تقسیم
اسم کے معنی، نوعیت اور استعمال کی بنیاد پر کی جاتی ہے۔ اسم کی تمام اہم اقسام درج ذیل ہیں
1. اسم ذات: وہ اسم جو کسی شخص، جگہ ، یا چیز کا خاص نام ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: علی، لاہور، کتاب، پانی۔
2. اسم صفت : وہ اسم جو کسی شخص، چیز، یا حالت کی خوبی یا وصف ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: خوبصورتی، اچھائی، تیزی، نرمی۔
3. اسم ضمیر: وہ اسم جو کسی اسم کی جگہ استعمال ہو ۔
مثال: میں ، تم ، وہ ، ہم، آپ۔
4. اسم عدد: وہ اسم جو مقدار یا تعداد کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: ایک، دو، تین، چار، پہلا ، دوسرا۔
5. اسم ظرف: وہ اسم جو وقت یا جگہ کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: کل، آج کل صبح، یہاں، وہاں۔
6. اسم آلہ : وہ اسم جو کسی کام کو انجام دینے کے لیے استعمال ہونے والے آلے کو ظاہر
کرے۔
مثال: قلم ، کتاب، ہتھوڑا، کمپیوٹر۔
7. اسم مجرو : وہ اسم جو غیر مادی یا مجر و چیزوں کو ظاہر کرے ۔
مثال: خوشی، غم، محبت، نفرت، امید ۔
8. اسم مرکب: دو یا زیادہ الفاظ کے مجموعے سے بننے والا اسم۔
مثال: پانی پت، سرخ مرچ ، گلاب جامن، دن رات ۔
9. اسم معرفہ : وہ اسم جو کسی خاص چیز، مشخص یا جگہ کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: علی، پاکستان، دریائے سندھ ۔
10. اسم نکرہ: دو اسم جو کسی عام چیز یا غیر معین چیز کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: لڑکا، دریا، شہر ، کتاب۔
11. اسم صوت: دو اسم جو کسی آواز یا آواز کی نقل کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال : تک تک (گھڑی کی آواز ) ، دھم (چیز گرنے کی آواز)، میاؤں ( بلی کی آواز )،
بھونک (کتنے کی آواز ) ۔
12. اسم کبیر: دو اسم جو کسی چیز یا حالت کو بڑھا چڑھا کر بیان کرے۔
مثال: بادشاہ (بڑا حکمران)، شهنشاه ( عظیم بادشاہ)، سمندر ( بہت بڑی مقدار میں
پانی)، پہاڑ ( بہت بڑی چٹان ) ۔
13. اسم موصوف : وہ اسم جس کی وضاحت کسی صفت سے کی جائے۔
مثال: خوبصورت لڑکی ، اونچا پہاڑ ، صاف پانی۔
14. اسم کیفیت : وہ اسم جو کسی حالت یا کیفیت کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال : سکون ، خوشی، غصہ، تھکاوٹ۔
15. اسم مجموعہ : وہ اسم جو کسی گروہ یا مجموعے کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: جماعت ، گردہ، لشکر ، ہجوم۔
16. اسم فعل: وہ اسم جو کسی فعل کا اثر ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: پڑھائی، روڑ ، سفر ، عبادت۔
17. اسم مصغر : وہ اسم جو کسی چیز یا ذات کو چھوٹا ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: بچہ (چھوٹا لڑکا)، کلی (چھوٹا پھول)، ٹہنی (چھوٹی شاخ)۔
18. اسم منسوب: وہ اسم جو کسی جگہ ، قوم، یا چیز سے نسبت ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: پاکستانی، ہندوستانی، لاہوری۔
19. اسم مجموعی : و و اسم جو کسی چیز کی مجموعی حالت کو ظاہر کرہے۔
مثال : جنگانات، پہاڑیاں، کھیت ۔
20. اسم اشخاص و اسم جو کسی خاص شخص کے نام کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: احمد ، فاطمہ ، زینب ، علی۔
21. اسم اماکن : وہ اسم جو کسی خاص جگہ یا مقام کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: کراچی، مسجد ، اسکول، دریا۔
22. اسم زمانی: وہ اسم جو کسی وقت یا زمانے کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: صبح ، شام ، رات، سال۔
23. اسم جسمانی : وہ اسم جو جسم کے حصو کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: ہاتھ ، پاؤں، سر ، دل۔
24. اسم غیر ذوی العقول: وہ اسم جو جاندار چیزوں کے علاوہ دیگر اشیاء کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: کتاب، پتھر، میز ، دیوار ۔

مثال: ہیں کھانا کھانا، بات کرنا، سکول جانا۔

فعل تام: وہ فعل جو اپنی ساخت میں مکمل ہو اور اضافی الفاظ کی ضرورت نہ ہو ۔ آئے، جملہ با معنی نہ بنے، کہا اتا ہے: (فعل متعدی)
مثال: وہ آیا، احمد بھاگا۔
.19 فعل جاریہ : وہ فعل جو کسی کام کے تسلسل یا جاری رہنے کو ظاہر کرے ۔
مثال : وہ کھیل رہا ہے ، ہم پڑھ رہے ہیں۔
.20 فعل حادثہ: وہ فعل جو کسی اچانک ہونے والے واقعے یا حالت کو ظاہر کرے ۔
مثال : در واز و ٹوٹ گیا، بر تن گر گیا۔

(بہادر شاہ ظفر)

.92 سید الشہدا قواعد کی رو سے کیا ہے ؟ (لقب)
اردو گرامر میں فعل (Verb) کی مختلف اقسام ہیں، جو فعل کے معنی، ساخت، اور استعمال کی
بنیاد پر تقسیم کی گئی ہیں۔ یہ تمام اقسام فعل کی گہرائی اور مختلف استعمال کو ظاہر کرتی ہیں اور
اردو گرامر کو سمجھنے میں مددگار ہیں۔ تفصیل درج ذیل ہے:
1 . فعل لازم: وہ فعل جو مفعول کے بغیر مکمل ہو جائے اور جملہ بامعنی رہے۔
مثال: لڑکا سو گیا، پرندہ اڑ گیا۔
2 . فعل متعدی: وہ فعل جو مفعول کے بغیر نامکمل ہو اور جملے کا مطلب پورا نہ ہو ۔
مثال: علی نے کتاب پڑھی، بچے نے کھانا کھایا۔
3 فعل معروف: وہ فعل جس میں فاعل کا ذکر واضح ہو اور جملے میں فاعل پر زور دیا جائے۔
مثال: علی نے خط لکھا، احمد نے پانی پیا۔
4 . فعل مجہول: وہ فعل جس میں فاعل کا ذکر نہ ہو بلکہ زور مفعول پر ہو۔
مثال : خط لکھا گیا، کھانا کھایا گیا۔
5 فعل حال : وہ فعل جو حالیہ وقت یا موجودہ حالت کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: وہ کھیل رہا ہے ، وہ پڑھتی ہے۔
6. فعل ماضی : وہ فعل جو کسی کام یا واقعے کے گزر جانے کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال: وہ سکول گیا، میں نے کتاب پڑھی۔
7. فعل مستقبل: وہ فعل جو آئندہ وقت میں کسی کام یا حالت کو ظاہر کرے۔
مثال : وہ سکول جائے گا، میں کتاب پڑھوں گا۔
8 فعل صیغہ واحد : وہ فعل جو واحد فاعل کے لیے استعمال ہو ۔
مثال: لڑکا دوڑ رہا ہے، احمد سویا۔
9 فعل صیغہ جمع : وہ فعل جو جمع فاعل کے لیے استعمال ہو ۔
مثال: لڑکے کھیل رہے ہیں، وہ لوگ پڑھ رہے ہیں۔
10 فعل امر : وہ فعل جو حکم دینے یا درخواست کرنے کے لیے استعمال ہو۔
مثال: کتاب دور پانی پیو۔
11 فعل نہی: وہ فعل جو منع کرنے کے لیے استعمال ہو۔
مثال: شور مت کرو، جھوٹ مت بولو۔
12 فعل معلوم : وہ فعل جس میں کام کرنے والے (فاعل) کی شناخت واضح ہو ۔
مثال : علی نے دروازہ کھولا ۔
13 فعل معین: وہ فعل جس میں فاعل کی حالت ، کام یا وقت کمل وضاحت کے ساتھ ظاہر
ہو ۔
مثال: وہ جلدی آرہا ہے۔
14 فعل ناقص : وہ فعل جو جملے کے معنی کو مکمل کرنے کے لیے کسی اور لفظ کا محتاج ہو۔
مثال: وہ بیمار لگ رہا ہے۔
15 فعل مکمل : وہ فعل جو جملے کے معنی کو بغیر کسی اضافی لفظ کے مکمل کر دے۔
مثال: وہ سویا، پرندہ اڑ گیا۔
16. فعل غیر متعدی: وہ فعل جو کسی مفعول کی ضرورت کے بغیر مکمل ہو جائے۔

Islamic Studies
93. How many Ansaar from Madinah embraced

Maeda)
95. What is the literal meaning of "Jihad"?
(Struggle)
96. The Holy Quran contains Makki and Madni
Surahs. The Madni Surahs have a generai
emphasis on: Ghazwat (Battles participated by
the Prophet (PBUH), Laws of nature, The
historical facts None of these)
Associated Information:
The Madni Surahs of the Quran generally focus on
building the Muslim community and providing guidance
on social, political, and legal matters. They often address
topics like:
• Laws of worship, family, trade, and governance.
• Rules for warfare, including the context of Ghazwat
(battles).
• Strengthening the Muslim Ummah.
• Refuting the People of the Book and addressing
their questions.
Although Madni Surahs contain references to battles
(Ghazwat), their primary focus is on community and legal
structure rather than solely on historical accounts of
battles..
Thus, the most precise answer would depend on what
aspect is emphasized in the question. If the question
specifically seeks the main thematic emphasis, it would
not solely be Ghazwat.
The revised correct answer: (D) None of these, as the
overarching themes go beyond these specific options.

20. The first British Viceroy of India was: (Lord
Canning)
Associated Information:
The position of Viceroy of India was created in 1858
following the Government of India Act 1858, which
marked the transfer of power from the East India
Company to the British Crown after the Indian War of
Independence, 1857. The Viceroy was the British
monarch's representative in India and held executive
authority over the country.
Lord Canning (1858-1862):
• First Viceroy: Appointed as the first Viceroy of India
in 1858, after serving as the Governor-General of
India since 1856.
• Major Achievements:
Oversaw the final suppression of the Indian War of
Independence, 1857.
Introduced key reforms, including the Indian Penal
Code and Code of Civil Procedure.
Initiated the policy of recognizing princely states.

--- Page 81 ---
Papers of 2019 81
Ο autonomous entities under British suzerainty.
Ο Played a key role in introducing the Doctrine of
Lapse for phased integration of princely states.
21. The Day of Deliverance was observed by All
India Muslim League on:
(A) 22nd December, 1939*
(B) 3rd June, 1947
(C) 23rd March, 1946
(D) 14th August, 1947
Associated Information:
The Day of Deliverance (Youm-e-Nijat) was observed by
the All-India Muslim League on 22nd December 1939
under the leadership of Muhammad Ali Jinnah, marking
a significant moment in pre-partition Indian politics.
Reason for Observance:
• The celebration was in response to the resignation of
all members of the Indian National Congress from
provincial and central offices.
• The Congress ministries had been functioning in most
provinces since 1937 but resigned in protest when the
British government declared India's entry into World
War II without consulting Indian leaders.
Why Did Congress Resign?
1. The Congress Working Committee opposed
Britain's unilateral decision to involve India in World
War II without prior consultation.
2. Congress demanded:
Ο The formation of a central Indian national
government.
Ο A guarantee of India's independence after the war.
3. When their demands were ignored, the Congress
ministries, led by leaders like Jawaharlal Nehru,
resigned in protest in October 1939.
Jinnah's Appeal:
• On 2nd December 1939, Muhammad Ali Jinnah
called for Indian Muslims to celebrate 22nd
December 1939 as the "Day of Deliverance".
• Jinnah described the resignation of Congress
ministries as a relief, calling it an end to what he saw
as the tyrannical Congress regime, which,
according to him, marginalized Muslims and
undermined their rights.
Observance of the Day:
• Public meetings were organized across India.
• Muslims offered prayers of thanksgiving after
Friday prayers to express gratitude for the end of
Congress rule.
• The day symbolized the Muslim League's increasing
dissent against the Congress and further solidified
the division between the two major political
entities.
Significance in Indian History:
• The Day of Deliverance marked a turning point in
the relationship between the All-India Muslim
League and the Indian National Congress.
• It highlighted the deepening communal and
political divide, setting the stage for the League's
later demands for Pakistan as a separate state for
Muslims.

36. Pakistan's National Anthem was approved by
the Government in: (1954)
Associated Information:
Pakistan's National Anthem: "Qaumi Tarānah"
Title: "Qaumi Taranah" (قومی ترانه)
Lyrics: Written by Hafeez Jullundhri in 1952
Music: Composed by Ahmed Ghulamali Chagla in 1949
Adopted: As the national anthem on August 14, 1954
First played: February 1950, before the King of Iran,
Mohammad Reza Pahlavi, during his visit to Karachi,
Pakistan
Language: Urdu, with Persian influences
Meaning: The anthem is a prayer for the country's.
prosperity and unity
Structure: Consists of three stanzas, with a total of 26
lines
Duration: Approximately 1 minute and 20 seconds
Instruments: Typically performed with a combination of
eastern and western instruments
Significance: Represents Pakistan's commitment to
Islam, democracy, and national unity
History:

--- Page 82 ---
82 Advanced PPSC MCQs Papers (Volume 2)
- February 1949: Government of Pakistan formed a
committee to prepare Pakistan's National Anthem. Out
of 723 people who competed, Hafeez Jalandhari's lyrics
were selected.
- 1949: Ahmed Ghulamali Chagla composed the music
- 1952: Hafeez Jullundhri wrote the lyrics
- February 1950: First played before the King of Iran
- August 14, 1954: Officially adopted as the national
anthem
Note: The lyrics were written by Hafeez Jullundhri In
1952, but the anthem was first played on March 1, 1950.
This means that The tune was then played without lyrics
on March 1, 1950, during the Shah of Iran's visit to
Pakistan. Later, Hafeez Jullundhri wrote the lyrics In
1952, and the complete anthem (tune and lyrics) was
officially adopted on August 14, 1954.
Selection Process:
- Committee formed in 1949 to select the national
anthem
- 723 people competed to write the National Anthem
- Hafeez Jalandhari's lyrics were selected as the national
anthem of Pakistan
- Tune selection process:
- 6 tunes were shortlisted from over 100 submissions
- Ahmed Ghulam Ali Chagla's tune was selected as the
final tune
- The duration of the National Anthem is 1 minute and
20 seconds (80 seconds).
First Recording:
- Recorded by a group of renowned singers in 1954
- The recording was done in a single take, with all the
singers performing together in the studio
- The leading singer of the group that recorded the
Pakistani national anthem in 1954 was Ahmed Rushdi.
He was a well-known playback singer and music
composer in Pakistan, and his powerful and soulful voice
was considered ideal for rendering the national anthem.
Rushdi was joined by a group of other renowned singers,
including Najam Ara, Naseema Shaheen, Zawar Hussain,
Akhtar Abbas, Ghulam Dastagir, Anwar Zaheer, Akhtar
Wasi Ali, Kaukab Jahan, Rasheeda Begum, and Shamim
Bano, to create a memorable and iconic recording of the
national anthem.
- This recording was done under the supervision of the
National Anthem Committee, which was responsible for
selecting the final version of the anthem
- The recording was done in the Pakistan Broadcasting
Corporation (PBC) studios in Karachi. Task of recording
was given to EMI.
- The recording has been preserved and is still used today
as the official version of the national anthem
- No other official recording of the national anthem has
been made since then, making this the only official
recording to date.
Summary:
Pakistan's national anthem, "Qaumi Tarānah", was
written by Hafeez Jullundhri in 1952 and composed by
Ahmed Ghulamali Chagla in 1949. It was adopted as the
national anthem on August 14, 1954, and first played
before the King of Iran in February 1950. The anthem has
a unique blend of Persian and Urdu languages and is
considered one of the most melodious and harmonious
anthems in the world. The recording of the anthem was
done by a group of renowned singers in 1954 and is still
used today as the official version.

Everyday Science
50. Which among the following is the best
conductor of electricity? (Silver)
Associated Information:
Silver is the best conductor of electricity due to its
exceptional electrical conductivity. This is measured by
the material's ability to transfer an electric current
efficiently. Silver's conductivity is the highest among all
metals, making it the best choice for applications
requiring minimal resistance.
Key Properties of Silver's Electrical Conductivity:
1. High Number of Free Electrons: Silver has a large
number of free electrons, which are not bound to
specific atoms and are free to move within the
material, facilitating current flow.
2. High Mobility of Electrons: The free electrons in
silver have high mobility, meaning they can move
quickly and easily through the material, reducing
resistance.


--- Page 1 ---
3. Crystal Structure: Silver's face-centered cubic (FCC)
crystal structure is highly efficient for electron
transfer, enabling smooth and uninterrupted
current flow.
Comparison of Electrical Conductivity (at Room
Temperature):
Material Conductivity (Siemens per meter, S/m)
Silver 6.3 x 10⁷ S/m
Copper 5.96 x 10⁷ S/m
Aluminum 3.45 x 10⁷ S/m
Steel 1.04 x 10⁶ S/m (varies by type of steel)
Why Silver is the Best Conductor:
1. Conductivity: Silver outperforms other metals due
to its unmatched ability to conduct electricity.
2. Comparison to Copper: While copper is widely used
in electrical wiring due to its lower cost, silver's
conductivity is slightly higher (approximately 5%
better).
3. Aluminum and Steel: Aluminum, although lighter
and cheaper, has lower conductivity than both
silver and copper.
4. Steel is a poor conductor compared to these metals
and is rarely used in applications requiring high
conductivity.

x-4=9
x=9+4
x = 13
x² = (13)²
x² = 169
x²-4 = 169-4
x²-4 = 165

97. The portion of the wall of Kaba, which is
between its door and Hajr-e-Aswad is called
(Al Multazim)
Associated Information:
The Kaaba, a cube-shaped building in Mecca, Saudi
Arabia, is the holiest site in Islam. Its significance is
profound, serving as the focal point for Muslims
worldwide during their prayers. The Kaaba's walls and
corners hold rich history and symbolism, adding depth to
its spiritual importance.
Walls of the Kaaba:
- Hatim (Hijr Ismail): The semi-circular wall adjacent to
the Kaaba, believed to be the original construction site
by Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham) and his son Ismail
(Ishmael).
- Wall of the Black Stone (Rukn al-Aswad): The eastern
wall featuring the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad).
- Yemeni Wall (Rukn al-Yamani): The southern wall
facing Yemen.

--- Page 3 ---
- Syrian Wall (Rukn al-Shami): The northern wall, facing
Syria and Türkiye.
- Iraqi Wall (Rukn al-'Iraqi): The eastern wall, facing Iraq.
Corners of the Kaaba:
- Rukn al-Aswad (Black Stone Corner): The eastern corner
featuring the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad), a heavenly
stone brought by angel Gabriel to Prophet Ibrahim.
Pilgrims touch or kiss it during Hajj as an act of devotion.
- Rukn al-Yamani (Yemeni Corner): Located on the
southern side, facing Yemen, pilgrims touch this corner
during circumambulation (tawaf).
- Rukn al-Shami (Syrian Corner): Positioned on the
northern side, facing Syria and Türkiye, this corner
symbolizes the unity of the Muslim ummah (community)
across geographical boundaries. Pilgrims touch it during
tawaf.
- Rukn al-'Iraqi (Iraqi Corner): The eastern corner, facing
Iraq, completes the set. Pilgrims touch or point towards
it during their tawaf.
98. Which is the seventh month of Islamic year?
(Rajab)
Associated Information:
The Islamic year, also known as the Hijri year, consists of
12 months. Here are the names of the months in the
Islamic calendar:
1. Muharram (محرم), 2. Safar (صفر), 3. Rabi' al-awwal (ربیع
الاول), 4. Rabi' ath-thani (ربیع الثانی), 5. Jumada al-awwal
(جمادی الاول), 6. Jumada ath-thani (جمادی الثانی), 7. Rajab (رجب),
8. Sha'ban (شعبان), 9. Ramadan (رمضان), 10. Shawwal (شوال),
11. Dhu al-Qadah (ذو القعده), 12. Dhu al-Hijjah (ذو الحجه).
Note that the Islamic calendar is a lunar calendar, so the
months are based on the phases of the moon. The
Islamic year is approximately 354 or 355 days long, which
is shorter than the solar year. As a result, the Islamic
months seem to shift relative to the solar calendar.

General Knowledge
1. Motto of Red Cross is: (Charity in War)
Associated Information:
The Red Cross is a humanitarian organization that
provides emergency assistance, disaster relief, and
education to individuals and communities around the
world. The organization is known for its:
- Neutral and impartial aid: Providing help regardless of
nationality, race, religion, or political affiliation.

Papers of 2019 73
- Protection of human life: Promoting respect for human
rights and international humanitarian law.
- Prevention of suffering: Alleviating human suffering in
times of war, disaster, and crisis.
- Volunteerism: Relying on dedicated volunteers to carry
out its mission.
Headquarters: Geneva, Switzerland (International
Committee of the Red Cross) and New York City, USA
(American Red Cross)
Some interesting facts about the Red Cross include:
- The organization was founded in 1863 by Henry Dunant
in Geneva, Switzerland.
- The Red Cross symbol is a reverse Swiss flag (white
cross on a red background).
- The organization has 192 member countries and 17
million volunteers worldwide.
- The Red Cross provides services such as blood
donation, first aid training, and disaster response.

Muslim Nobel Laureates (Updated to 2025):
As of 2026, thirteen Nobel Prize laureates have been

Additional Facts about the Nobel Prizes:
• Established: Through Alfred Nobel's will (1895).
• First Awarded: 1901.
• Categories: Physics, Chemistry, Medicine, Literature,
Peace, and Economic Sciences (added in 1968).
• Awarding Bodies:
- Physics & Chemistry: Royal Swedish Academy of
Sciences
- Medicine: Karolinska Institute
- Literature: Swedish Academy
- Peace: Norwegian Nobel Committee
- Economic Sciences: Royal Swedish Academy of
Sciences
• Award Ceremony: December 10 every year (Alfred
Nobel's death anniversary).
• Prize Value: As of 2024-25, 11 million SEK (~$1 million
USD).
• Multiple Laureates Example: ICRC has received the
Nobel Peace Prize three times.
• Posthumous Rule: Generally not awarded
posthumously, except if the laureate dies after the
announcement.
• Youngest Laureate: Malala Yousafzai (age 17, 2014).

• Oldest Laureate: Leonid Hurwicz (age 90, 2007,
Economics).

Associated Information:
Hillary Clinton's book Hard Choices was published in
2014. In this memoir, she provides an account of her
tenure as U.S. Secretary of State from 2009 to 2013,
detailing the critical decisions and challenges
encountered during her service.
Clinton has authored several other notable works:
• Living History (2003): A memoir reflecting on her
early life, time as First Lady, and experiences up to
her tenure as a U.S. Senator from New York.
• It Takes a Village (1996): Discusses the impact of
communities on child development and advocates
for societal support in raising children.
• What Happened (2017): Analyzes the 2016
presidential election, offering insights into her
campaign and the factors contributing to its
outcome.
• The Book of Gutsy Women (2019): Co-authored
with her daughter, Chelsea Clinton, this book
profiles women who have inspired them through
their courage and resilience.
• State of Terror (2021): A political thriller co-written
with author Louise Penny, marking Clinton's debut
in fiction.
• Something Lost, Something Gained (2024): Reflects
on life, love, politics, liberty, democracy, and the
future, offering candid views on these subjects.
Each of these works provides unique perspectives on her
personal experiences and views on various societal
issues.

The Second Constitution of Pakistan (the Constitution
of 1962) was promulgated on 1st March 1962 but came
into force on 8th June 1962.
To summarize:
• Promulgation date: 1st March 1962
• Enforcement date: 8th June 1962
25. The only Vice President in the history of

--- Page 5 ---
Pakistan was: (Nur-ul-Amin)
Associated Information:
The first and only Vice President in the history of
Pakistan was indeed Nurul Amin. He held this position
from December 20, 1971, to August 14, 1973, when the
post was abolished. Amin also played a significant role
during the Liberation War of Bangladesh. After
participating in the 1970 Pakistani general election, he
was appointed as the Prime Minister of Pakistan. His
tenure as Vice President remains a unique chapter in
Pakistan's political history.
Here are some more details about Nurul Amin's career:
- He was the eighth Prime Minister of Pakistan and
served from December 7 to December 20, 1971.
- He was the Chief Minister of East Bengal from
September 14, 1948, to April 3, 1954.
- He was the Leader of the Opposition from July 9, 1967,
to December 7, 1970.
- He was a member of the Muslim League and later
joined the Pakistan Muslim League.
Amin's political career was marked by significant events
in Pakistan's history, including the Bengali language
movement, the 1971 Liberation War, and the eventual
breakup of East Pakistan.

28. The largest Princely State by area at the time of
partition was: (Kashmir)
Associated Information:
• Jammu and Kashmir: A Single Princely State
○ Formation: Jammu and Kashmir, including Jammu,
Kashmir Valley, Ladakh, Gilgit, and Baltistan, was a
single princely state established in 1846 under the
Treaty of Amritsar. Maharaja Gulab Singh acquired
the region from the British.
○ Unified Administration: The Maharaja governed
all regions as one entity, despite their geographic
and cultural diversity.
○ Partition of 1947: At partition, Jammu and
Kashmir remained a unified princely state under
Maharaja Hari Singh, who had the choice to
accede to India, Pakistan, or remain independent.
○ Post-Partition Division: After the 1947-48 conflict:
India administered Jammu, the Kashmir Valley,
and Ladakh.
Pakistan controlled Azad Jammu and Kashmir (AJK)
and Gilgit-Baltistan, which were treated
separately.
Thus, historically, Jammu and Kashmir, including all its
regions, was a single state until partition-induced
divisions.
○ Comparison with Other Princely States:
○ Kashmir: 222,236 sq km
○ Hyderabad: 212,000 sq km
○ Bahawalpur: 45,911 sq km
○ Bhopal: 17,952 sq km

at: (Luckhnow)

Papers of 2019 87
30. Which party started Quit India Movement:
(Congress)
Associated Information:
The Quit India Movement (1942) was a significant event
in India's struggle for Independence from British colonial
rule. Mahatma Gandhi's "Do or Die" call to action
inspired millions to participate in nationwide protests,
strikes, and demonstrations. Women, students, and
youth played a crucial role in the movement, which was
met with repression from British authorities. Although
the movement was weakened by internal divisions and
did not immediately lead to independence, it
demonstrated India's resolve and paved the way for
eventual freedom in 1947.
31. The Mopla uprising/revolt in 1921 against the
British colonial power in India, was: (To lend
support to the Khilafat Movement)
Associated Information:
The Mopla Uprising of 1921 was a significant anti-
colonial revolt by the Mopla (or Moplah) Muslim
community of the Malabar region in southern India. The
primary cause of the uprising was their support for the
Khilafat Movement (Option C) and their resistance to
British colonial rule, combined with local grievances such
as socio-economic oppression by Hindu landlords.
The revolt began as part of the larger Khilafat and Non-
Cooperation Movements, which aimed to oppose British
imperialism and demand the restoration of the Ottoman
Caliphate. However, the uprising quickly escalated into a
violent conflict, with attacks on British officials and local
landlords. While initially rooted in anti-colonial
sentiment, the movement also took on communal
overtones.
The British responded with severe repression, deploying
military forces to crush the rebellion. Thousands of
Mopla participants were killed, imprisoned, or exiled,
making it one of the bloodiest episodes in India's
struggle for independence. The Mopla Uprising serves as
a reminder of the complex dynamics of local socio-
economic struggles intersecting with national
movements like the Khilafat campaign.

57. A father is twice as old as his son 20 years ago
the age of the father was, 12 times the age of
the son. The present age of the father is: (44
years)
Solution:
Let son age = x
Father age = 2x
12(x-20) = (2x - 20)
12x - 240 = 2x - 20
12x - 2x = 240 - 20
10x = 220
x = 220
10
x = 22
Father age
= 2 x 22
= 44

64. Which of the following is a binary number?
(1001)
Solution:
Binary Number
A binary number is a number that consists of only
two digits: 0 and 1. In this case, the number 1001
meets this criterion, making it a binary number.
The other options, 1002, 1005, and 1006, are not
binary numbers because they contain digits other
than 0 and 1.
Here's a brief explanation of each option:
- 1002: Contains the digit 2, which is not a binary
digit.
- 1005: Contains the digit 5, which is not a binary
digit.
- 1006: Contains the digit 6, which is not a binary
digit.

PAPER 13 JUNIOR CLERK

General Knowledge
1. IBRD Is another name of (World Bank)
Associated Information:
The International Bank for Reconstruction and
Development (IBRD) is part of the World Bank Group
and is commonly referred to as the World Bank in
broader contexts. Below is a detailed explanation and
historical background:
Bretton Woods Agreement
• Signed on July 22, 1944, In Bretton Woods, New
Hampshire, USA.
o Aimed to establish an international monetary and
economic order post-World War II.
o Created two key institutions:
• International Monetary Fund (IMF): To promote
global monetary cooperation and exchange rate
stability.
o World Bank (IBRD): To aid in reconstruction and
development of war-torn and underdeveloped
countries.
o Key objectives:
o Promote International monetary cooperation.
o Ensure exchange rate stability.
o Foster economic growth and development.
o Reduce poverty and Inequality globally.
o Introduced the US dollar as the global reserve
currency..
o Initially established a fixed exchange rate system
(later replaced by a floating system).
o Created Special Drawing Rights (SDRs) as a
supplementary foreign exchange reserve asset.
International Bank for Reconstruction and
Development (IBRD)
• Established:
o Agreement signed on July 22, 1944.
o Began operations on June 25, 1946.
• Focus:
o Provides loans and financial assistance to middle-
income and creditworthy low-income countries.
o Supports development projects such as
infrastructure, education, and healthcare.
• Institutions:
o Board of Governors
o Executive Directors
o World Bank Institute
o Research Departments
• Operates within the framework of the World Bank
Group.
World Bank
• Established alongside IBRD in 1944 and
operational since 1946.
o Encompasses the IBRD and four other
institutions:
o IDA (International Development Association):
Focused on the poorest countries.
o IFC (International Finance Corporation): Supports
private sector development.
o MIGA (Multilateral Investment Guarantee
Agency): Provides political risk insurance.
o ICSID (International Centre for Settlement of
Investment Disputes): Handles investment
disputes.
• Goals:
o Reduce poverty and increase shared prosperity.
o Promote sustainable development globally.
• Provides financial and technical assistance to
member countries.
Comparison of IBRD and World Bank
• IBRD:
o Part of the World Bank Group.
o Focuses on middle-income countries.
o Provides loans and financial assistance.
• World Bank (broader scope):
o Includes IBRD, IDA, and other institutions.
o Offers a wide range of financial and technical
assistance.
Key Distinction
• The IBRD is a specific agency within the World
Bank Group that focuses primarily on
reconstruction and development, while the term
"World Bank" often refers to the larger
organization, including all its affiliated agencies.
This foundational structure, established under the
Bretton Woods Agreement, remains critical to global
economic development efforts.
