8. OIC headquarters is in: (Jeddah)
Associated Information:
OIC (Organisation of Islamic Cooperation)
- Established in 1969
- Headquarters: Jeddah, Saudi Arabia

--- Page 91 ---
1
- 57 member states, most of which are Muslim-majority
countries
Reasons behind establishment:
- Solidarity among Muslim countries in response to the
1969 al-Aqsa Mosque fire in Jerusalem
- Countering the influence of colonial powers and
promoting independence
- Protecting and promoting Islamic values, principles,
and interests
- Supporting the Palestinian cause and the rights of
Muslim minorities
- Fostering economic cooperation, social justice, and
human development
Objectives:
- Promote Islamic values and principles
- Protect the rights of Muslim minorities
- Support Palestinian rights and sovereignty
• Encourage economic cooperation and development
- Strengthen social and cultural ties among member
states
Organs and institutions:
- Islamic Development Bank (IDB)
- Headquarters: Jeddah, Saudi Arabia
- Islamic Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization
(ISESCO)
- Headquarters: Rabat, Morocco
- OIC Human Rights Commission
- Headquarters: Jeddah, Saudi Arabia
Weaknesses and failures:
- Ineffective in addressing conflicts and human rights
issues in member states
- Failure to prevent wars and violence in Muslim-
majority countries (e.g. Syria, Yemen, Afghanistan)
- Limited economic cooperation and development
among member states
- Criticisms of human rights abuses in some member
states (e.g. Saudi Arabia, Iran)
- Political and ideological divisions among member states
(e.g. Sunni-Shia divide)
- Inability to address issues of terrorism and extremism
- Limited representation and empowerment of Muslim
minorities and women
- Inefficient decision-making processes and lack of
implementation of OIC resolutions

2. United States: Over 600,000 bridges, including the
world's busiest crossings.
3. Japan: Over 100,000 bridges, known for high-tech
earthquake-resistant designs.
Countries with the Most Bridges
1. China: Over 800,000 bridges (home to 4 of the top
record-breaking bridges), more than the combined
total of the United States, Japan, and Germany.
2. United States: Over 600,000 bridges, second only
to China, and home to the busiest bridge in the
world.
3. Japan: Over 100,000 bridges, renowned for its
advanced engineering and iconic suspension
bridges.

16. The world's largest undersea railway tunnel is

(Denmark and Germany)
Associated information:
Explore the advancements in undersea railway tunnels,
both existing and upcoming:
Notable Existing Undersea Tunnels:
1. Channel Tunnel (Eurotunnel):
o Record: Longest undersea portion (38 km).
o Details: Opened in 1994, this 50.45 km (31.35
miles) tunnel connects England and France under
the English Channel. Its undersea portion holds the
global record for length.
2. Seikan Tunnel:
o Record: Longest undersea tunnel by total length
(53.85 km).
o Details: Located in Japan, this tunnel connects
Honshu and Hokkaido, with 23.3 km (14.5 miles)
running underwater.
3. Marmaray Tunnel:
o Record: Deepest undersea tunnel (64 meters below
sea level).
o Details: This 13.5 km (8.4 miles) tunnel under the
Bosporus Strait in Istanbul connects Europe and
Asia for both rail and road traffic.
4. Öresund Tunnel (Öresundsbron):
o Record: Deepest immersed tube tunnel (35
meters).
o Details: Connecting Denmark and Sweden, this
tunnel is part of the Öresund Bridge, with an 8 km
immersed tube segment.
Upcoming Projects:
1. Baltic Sea Tunnel (Fehmarnbelt Tunnel):
o Record (Upon Completion): Longest immersed
undersea tunnel (18 km).
o Details: Under construction, it will connect
Denmark and Germany, facilitating road and rail
traffic.
2. Hong Kong-Zhuhai-Macau Bridge Tunnel:
o Record (Upon Completion): Longest undersea
tunnel in China (6.7 km).
o Details: This tunnel will strengthen regional
connectivity in southern China.
Significance: These tunnels not only represent
engineering marvels but also play a vital role in
enhancing international connectivity, trade, and travel.
The Baltic Sea Tunnel between Denmark and Germany
is set to break new records upon completion.

37. Muhammad Ali Jauhar younger brother of

38. Partition of Bengal was annulled after: (6 years)
Associated Information:
The Partition of Bengal (1905) was a significant and
controversial event in Indian history during the British
colonial period. Implemented on October 16, 1905,
under the administration of Lord Curzon, it led to
widespread protests and eventually its annulment in
1911, six years later.
Background:
Ο Bengal's Size and Composition:
At the time, Bengal was one of the largest
provinces in British India, encompassing present-day
Bangladesh, West Bengal, and parts of neighboring
regions.
Ο Its vastness made administration and governance
challenging for the British.
Ο Partition Plan:
Bengal was divided into two provinces:
1. Eastern Bengal and Assam (Capital: Dhaka).
2. Western Bengal (Capital: Calcutta), later known as
Bengal (comprising Western Bengal, Bihar, and
Orissa).
Ο Muslim Leadership: Prominent leaders like Nawab
Salimullah Khan supported the partition as it provided
political and educational advantages to Muslims in East
Bengal.
Reasons for Partition:
1. Administrative Convenience: The British argued
that Bengal was too large to be governed effectively
as a single entity.
2. Divide and Rule: Critics believe the partition aimed
to create divisions between Hindus and Muslims to
weaken the growing unity among Indians against
colonial rule.
Consequences:
1. Hindu Opposition: Hindu Bengalis, especially from
Calcutta, strongly opposed the partition, viewing it
as an attempt to curtail their influence. Prominent
leaders like Rabindranath Tagore and
Surendranath Banerjee spearheaded the
opposition.
2. Swadeshi Movement: The partition ignited the
Swadeshi Movement, urging Indians to boycott
British goods and promote indigenous industries.
3. Economic and Social Disruption: The division
disrupted Bengal's trade networks and social
structures, further intensifying protests.
4. Muslim Support: Many Muslims in Eastern Bengal
supported the partition as it created a province
where they were a majority, fostering educational
and economic opportunities.
Reversal of Partition:
1. Annulment in 1911: Six years after its
implementation, the Partition of Bengal was
annulled on the occasion of King George V's
2. coronation as Emperor of India during his visit to
Delhi.
Reorganization: Bengal was reunited, but Bihar and
Orissa were separated to form a new province. The
capital of British India was shifted from Calcutta to
Delhi to appease nationalist sentiments and reduce
the prominence of Bengal in the independence
movement.
3. Impact on Communities: The annulment was seen
as a victory for Hindus who had opposed the
partition. Conversely, it was viewed as a setback for
Muslims, who had benefitted from the division and
saw it as recognition of their distinct political
identity.
Significance:
Ο The Partition of Bengal remains a pivotal event in
India's colonial history. It highlighted:
Ο British Divide-and-Rule Policies: Efforts to exploit
religious divisions for political control.
Ο Growing Nationalism: The emergence of mass
movements like the Swadeshi Movement.
Ο Hindu-Muslim Dynamics: Differing reactions to the
partition underscored evolving communal
identities.
By uniting Bengal in 1911, the British aimed to quell
discontent, but the event left lasting implications for
India's independence struggle.

51. Benjamin Franklin due to his invention of

Associated Information:
Benjamin Franklin was an American polymath and one of
the most influential Founding Fathers of the United
States. His contributions spanned science, politics, and
social reforms.
Roles and Accomplishments
Ο Printer and Writer: A successful printer and
publisher, Franklin authored "Poor Richard's
Almanack" and his widely read autobiography.
Ο Scientist and Inventor: Known for pioneering
experiments and inventions.
Ο Statesman:
Ο Played a leading role in drafting the United States
Declaration of Independence and the United
States Constitution.
Ο Served as Postmaster General, Minister to France,
and Governor of Pennsylvania.
Scientific Contributions and Inventions
1. Lightning Rod (1752):
Ο Conducted his famous kite experiment, proving
that lightning is a form of electricity.
Ο Developed the lightning rod to protect buildings
and ships from lightning strikes, earning him the
title "Father of Electricity."
2. Bifocal Glasses (1784): Revolutionized vision
correction for individuals needing assistance with
both near and far vision.
3. Franklin Stove (1741): A more efficient wood-
burning stove for heating homes.
4. Postal System Improvements: Streamlined postal
operations in the American colonies.
5. Swim Fins (1717): Invented at the age of 11 to aid
in swimming.
6. Glass Harmonica (1761): A musical instrument
producing ethereal tones.
7. Odometer (1763): Used to measure distances for
postal routes.
Electrical Experiments
• Conducted groundbreaking experiments with
electricity, leading to fundamental discoveries
such as:
Ο Differentiating positive and negative charges.
Ο Introducing terms like battery, conductor, and
capacitor.
Ο His experiments culminated in the understanding
of the nature of electricity, shaping the foundation
of modern electrical science.
Philosophy and Wit
• Known for his wisdom and aphorisms, Franklin
coined numerous popular sayings, such as:
Papers of 2019 95
Ο "Early to bed and early to rise, makes a man
healthy, wealthy, and wise."
Ο "An investment in knowledge pays the best
interest."
• His writings, particularly his autobiography,
provide valuable insights into his life, philosophy,
and the times he lived in.

55. Which unit is used to measure latitudes of
earth? (Degrees)
Associated Information:
Latitudes and longitudes are measured in the following
units:
- Latitude:
    - Degrees (°)
    - Minutes (')
    - Seconds (")
- Longitude:
    - Degrees (°)
    - Minutes (')
    - Seconds (")
Note:
- 1 degree = 60 minutes
- 1 minute = 60 seconds
Also, latitudes are measured from 0° to 90° North (N) or
South (S), while longitudes are measured from 0° to 180°
East (E) or West (W).
Additionally, modern mapping and navigation systems
often use decimal degrees (DD) format, which expresses
latitudes and longitudes as a single value in decimal
format, such as:
- Latitude: 34.0522° N
- Longitude: 118.2437° W
This format is commonly used in GPS coordinates and
online mapping applications.

61. First generation computer used which

Associated Information:
Here are the generations of computers, including the
programming languages they typically used:
1. First Generation (1946-1959): Vacuum Tubes

--- Page 96 ---
96 Advanced PPSC MCQs Papers (Volume 2)
- Characteristics: Large size, high power consumption,
unreliable
- Examples: ENIAC, UNIVAC
- Languages: Machine language, Assembly language
(e.g., Short Code, Symbolic Optimal Assembly Program)
2. Second Generation (1959-1965): Transistors
- Characteristics: Smaller size, lower power
consumption, faster
- Examples: IBM 1401, PDP-8
- Languages: Assembly language (e.g., COBOL,
FORTRAN, ALGOL)
3. Third Generation (1965-1971): Integrated Circuits
- Characteristics: Even smaller size, lower power
consumption, faster
- Examples: IBM System/360, PDP-11
- Languages: High-level languages (e.g., C, C++, PL/1,
BASIC)
4. Fourth Generation (1971-1980): Microprocessors
- Characteristics: Personal computing, lower cost,
higher performance
- Examples: Intel 4004, Apple I
- Languages: High-level languages (e.g., Pascal, C,
CP/M, Apple DOS)
5. Fifth Generation (1980-present): Artificial Intelligence
and Beyond
- Characteristics: AI, machine learning, natural
language processing, parallel processing
- Examples: Modern computers, smartphones, tablets,
and laptops
- Languages: High-level languages (e.g., Python, Java,
JavaScript, C++), AI-specific languages (e.g., Prolog, LISP),
and scripting languages (e.g., Ruby, PHP)
Note that this is not an exhaustive list of languages, but
rather a selection of examples to illustrate the
progression of programming languages alongside
computer generations.

Basic Mathematics

66. In a zoo there are Rabbits and Pigeons. If
heads are counted there are 200 and if legs are
counted, there are 580. How many pigeons are
there? (110)
Solution:
Rabbits = x
Pigeons = y
Heads = 200
Legs = 580
x + y = 200 ...(i)
4x + 2y = 580
2(2x + y) = 580
2x + y = 290 ...(ii)
Subtract eq (i) and (ii)
2x + y - x - y = 290 - 200
x = 90
Put in (i)
90 + y = 200
y = 200 - 90
y = 110
67. In a school having roll strength 286 the ratio of
boys and girls is 8:5. If 22 more girls get
admitted into the school, the ratio of boys and
girls becomes: (4:3)
Solution:
Boy = 8x
Girls = 5x
Total = 286
8x + 5x = 286
13x = 286
x = 286/13
x = 22
8x = 8 x 22
= 176.
5x = 5 x 22
= 110
No. of boys = 176
No. of girls = 110
After adding 22 girls
= 110 + 22 = 132.
Ratio boys to girls = 176 : 132
= 88 : 66
= 8 : 6
= 4 : 3
68. If 3 is a solution of 3x^2 + (k − 1) x + 9 = 0.
then k = ? (-11)
Solution:
3x² + (k-1)x + 9 = 0
Put x = 3.
3(3)² + (k-1)3 + 9 = 0
27 + 3k - 3 + 9 = 0
27 + 3k + 6 = 0
3k + 33 = 0
3k = -33
k = -33/3
k = -11
69. X^2 > y^2 then possible solution is: (X is
greater than Y)
Explanation:
Since X^2 > Y^2, we can take the square root of both
sides:
√(X^2) > √(Y^2)
This simplifies to:
|X| > |Y|
Since the absolute value of X is greater than the
absolute value of Y, we can conclude that X is
greater than Y.
Note that this assumes that X and Y are real
numbers. If X and Y are complex numbers, the

--- Page 97 ---
Papers of 2019 97
situation is more complicated, and the conclusion
might not hold.
So, the correct answer is (A) X is greater than Y.

71. Solve the series 2, 4, 8, 16, ... (32)
Solution:
2, 4, 8, 16, 32
×2 ×2 ×2 ×2
2 x 2 = 4
4 x 2 = 8
8 x 2 = 16
16 x 2 = 32

77. Change the voice: He asked me if I could drive
a car. (I was asked I could drive a car)
Explanation:
In passive voice, the subject and object switch positions
while maintaining the original meaning. The sentence
"He asked me if I could drive a car" changes to "I was
asked if I could drive a car" to retain the grammatical
structure and intent.

96. The word Namaz is repeated for how many
times in the Holy Quran? (500 times)
Explanation: The word "Salah" appears 67-83
times in the Qur'an, depending on whether noun forms
alone or all derivatives are counted. Claims of 500+ times
are debatable, often due to confusion with the root s-l-
w or general prayer references.
Scholarly references confirm:
Dr. Mustafa Khattab (The Clear Quran): 99 times
(including derivatives)
Abdul Haleem (Oxford Quran): 82 direct mentions
Journal of Quranic Studies: Rejects counts above 100
The "500 times" figure persists due to South Asia, where
the term Namaz is loosely applied.
Conclusion: All options (A-D) are incorrect; verified
count is 82-99.

Associated Information:
Best Tennis Players
Men's Tennis:
Novak Djokovic (Serbian): 24 Grand Slam titles, seven
ATP Finals crowns, and 40 ATP Masters 1000 crowns.
Rafael Nadal (Spanish): 22 Grand Slam titles and a
record 14 French Open titles.
Roger Federer (Swiss): 20 Grand Slam titles and held the
world No. 1 spot for 310 weeks during his career.
Rod Laver (Australian): 11 Grand Slam singles titles and
the only player to have won the Grand Slam (all four
majors in a single year) twice.
Pete Sampras (American): 14 Grand Slam singles titles
and held the world No. 1 ranking for six consecutive
years.
Bjorn Borg (Swedish): 11 Grand Slam singles titles, all at
Wimbledon and the French Open.
Ivan Lendl (Czech-American): 8 Grand Slam singles titles
and was the world's top-ranked player for four years.
Jimmy Connors (American): 8 Grand Slam singles titles
and holds the record for most ATP tour titles (109).
John McEnroe (American): 7 Grand Slam singles titles,
known for his creative shot-making and doubles success.
Andre Agassi (American): 8 Grand Slam singles titles and
an Olympic Gold Medalist (1996).
Ken Rosewall (Australian): 8 Grand Slam singles titles
and inducted into the Tennis Hall of Fame in 1980.
Women's Tennis:
Serena Williams (American): 23 Grand Slam singles titles
and 14 Grand Slam doubles titles.
Martina Hingis (Swiss): 12 singles titles, 12 women's
doubles titles, and one mixed doubles title.
Steffi Graf (German): 22 Grand Slam singles titles and
the only player to achieve the Golden Slam (all four
majors and Olympic Gold in a single year).
Chris Evert (American): 157 singles titles and widely
regarded as one of the greatest tennis players of all time.
Billie Jean King (American): 129 singles titles and a
pioneer for women's tennis.
Note: Some players may have multiple nationalities or
have represented different countries during their
careers, but the most commonly associated nationality
has been listed.

many notable tragedies and comedies. His tragedies
include Titus Andronicus, Romeo and Juliet, Julius
Caesar, Hamlet, Othello, King Lear, Macbeth, and
Antony and Cleopatra. Among his celebrated comedies
are The Two Gentlemen of Verona, The Taming of the
Shrew, The Comedy of Errors, Love's Labour's Lost, A
Midsummer Night's Dream, The Merchant of Venice,
Much Ado About Nothing, Twelfth Night, and As You
Like It.
"Arms and the Man" is a play written by George Bernard
Shaw, not William Shakespeare.

Pakistan Studies
27. Rohtas Fort is 8 km from Dina. It was built by:
(Sher Shah Suri)
28. The largest fort of Asia is Ranikot Fort. It is
located near
(Jamshoro)
Associated Information: Ranikot Fort - The Largest Fort
in the World
Ranikot Fort - Jamshoro, Sindh: Ranikot Fort is the
largest fort in the world, covering a total area of
29,000,000 square meters (7,800 hectares or 19,200
acres), with a 35-kilometer-long wall. Built in the 17th
century by the Talpur rulers, this fort is considered
unique due to its strategic defense, vast expanse, and
historical significance.
Difference Between Forts and Castles in the
Subcontinent
All major defensive structures built in the Indian
subcontinent were forts, not castles. In Europe, castles
were built as royal residences, featuring decorative
buildings, gardens, and luxury arrangements. In contrast,
forts in the subcontinent were purely military
structures, designed for defense, border surveillance,
and protection against invasions. While some forts
housed royal residences, their primary function was
military.
Major Forts in Pakistan - Defensive Military Structures
1. Lahore Fort - Lahore, Punjab: Built in the 16th
century by Mughal Emperor Akbar, this UNESCO World
Heritage Site includes Sheesh Mahal, Diwan-e-Khas,
and royal residences, though its primary purpose was
defense.
2. Rohtas Fort - Jhelum, Punjab: Constructed in the
16th century by Sher Shah Suri for military defense,
without any royal residence, to prevent Mughal
Invasions.
3. Attock Fort - Attock, Punjab: Built in the 16th
century by Mughal Emperor Akbar to secure the
northwestern border.
4. Multan Fort - Multan, Punjab: Originally built by
the Hindu Katoch dynasty in the 17th century, it was
later conquered by Mughal Emperor Akbar in 1557.
5. Baltit Fort - Karimabad, Gilgit-Baltistan:
Constructed in the 13th century by local rulers and later
converted into a mosque in the 16th century.
6. Altit Fort - Gilgit-Baltistan: Built in the 13th
century by the rulers of Hunza for trade and defense
purposes.
7. Umerkot Fort - Umerkot, Sindh: A 16th-century
fort, famously known as the birthplace of Mughal
Emperor Akbar.
8. Kohat Fort - Kohat, Khyber Pakhtunkhwa: Built by
the British in the 19th century for military purposes.
9. Bala Hissar Fort - Peshawar, Khyber Pakhtunkhwa:
Constructed by Ahmad Shah Durrani in the 19th
century, serving as a strategic military stronghold.
Other Large Forts in the World
• Chittorgarh Fort - India: Spanning 2,800,000
square meters, it is a massive defensive fort.
• Mehrangarh Fort - India: Covering 81,227 square
meters, it is famous for its strong fortifications.
• Rohtas Fort - Pakistan: A 16th-century fort built for
military defense.
Famous Castles in the World
• Malbork Castle - Poland: With an area of 143,591
square meters, it is the largest castle in the world.
• Prague Castle - Czech Republic: Covering 66,761.
square meters, it is one of Europe's largest castles.
• Windsor Castle - England: Spanning 54,835 square
meters, it serves as a residence of the British royal
family.
Conclusion: Ranikot Fort is the largest fort in the world,
covering 29,000,000 square meters, making it larger
than any other fort. All forts in the Indian subcontinent
were built for defense, and there were no European-
style castles. While Lahore Fort and other forts housed
royal residences, they were still classified as forts, not
castles.
If we compare the world's largest forts, Ranikot Fort
ranks first. However, if castles are included, Malbork
Castle in Poland, with an area of 143,591 square
meters, is considered the largest castle in the world.

33. Who is the father of civil services in India?
(Charles Cornwallis)
Associated Information:
Warren Hastings, the first Governor-General of Bengal
(1773-1785), laid the foundation for British India's
administration by introducing key reforms and
establishing institutions like the Calcutta Madrasa and
the Sanskrit College. However, the title "Father of Civil
Services in India" is attributed to Charles Cornwallis.
Cornwallis, as Governor-General (1786-1793),
professionalized the civil services by implementing
merit-based recruitment and training, distinguishing
between covenanted and uncovenanted services, and
streamlining legal procedures. His systematic reforms
made the civil services more efficient and structured,
earning the recognition as the father of India's civil
service.

Geography
51. Glaciers are large deposits of ice. They are
found in: (None of the above)
Associated Information:
Glaciers are massive, slow-moving bodies of ice found on
every continent except Australia, primarily in polar
regions and high-altitude mountain ranges such as the
Himalayas (Pakistan, India, Nepal, Bhutan), the Andes
(Chile, Argentina, Peru, Bolivia), the Alps, the Rockies,
East Africa (Tanzania, Kenya, Uganda), Mexico, and New
Guinea. According to the Randolph Glacier Inventory
(RGI Version 6.0, 2017) - the internationally accepted
global glacier database used in IPCC assessments -
glaciers are currently documented in 44 countries
worldwide. This inventory is based on satellite imagery
and standardized glacier definitions, making it the most
reliable scientific source for global glacier distribution.
The World Glacier Monitoring Service (WGMS), hosted
at the University of Zurich, compiles long-term glacier
monitoring data from dozens of countries and operates
within the RGI scientific framework. Although WGMS
does not independently determine the total number of
glacier-hosting countries, its data align with the RGI
classification.
Earlier educational sources sometimes cited figures
ranging from 47 to 50 countries. However, improved
satellite mapping, refined glacier definitions, and
updated glaciological analysis have standardized the
scientifically supported number to 44 countries.
52. Roof of the world is the title of top world plain.
(Pamir)
Associated Information:
The Pamir Plateau, often called the "Roof of the World",
is a high-altitude plain located in Central Asia,
specifically in Tajikistan, with parts extending into
Afghanistan, China, and Kyrgyzstan. It is a crucial
geographical feature where several major mountain
ranges converge, including:
• The Himalayas
• The Karakoram
• The Hindu Kush
• The Tian Shan
South Asia and Its Mountain Ranges
1. The Himalayas:
o Primarily located in India, Nepal, Bhutan, and
Pakistan, with a northern extension into Tibet
(China).

--- Page 101 ---
Papers of 2019
101
o Includes Mount Everest (8,848.86 m), the world's
highest peak.
2. The Karakoram:
o Spanning Pakistan, India, and China, the
Karakoram range is an essential feature of South
Asia.
o Home to K2 (8,611 m), the second-highest peak in
the world.
3. The Hindu Kush:
o Predominantly in Afghanistan and Pakistan, the
Hindu Kush is closely linked to South Asia
geographically and historically.
Pamir Plateau's Connection to South Asia
The Pamir Plateau lies at the intersection of South Asia
and Central Asia, linking the mountain ranges of South
Asia (Himalayas, Karakoram, Hindu Kush) to Central Asia.
While geographically part of Central Asia, its proximity
to these South Asian ranges and its role as a historical
corridor (e.g., the Silk Road) make it a shared natural
feature between these regions.
Clarification about "Roof of the World":
The title "Roof of the World" is traditionally attributed
to the Pamir Plateau due to its extreme altitude and
significance. However, the term has also been loosely
applied to other high-altitude features, such as the
Karakoram Highway (KKH).
• The Karakoram Highway traverses the Himalayas
and Karakoram ranges, reaching altitudes of over
4,700 meters (15,400 feet), making it the highest
paved international road.
• This association adds another dimension to the
"Roof of the World" title, often linked to regions of
exceptional altitude and significance.

63. Study of ancestors, family history and tracing
their lineage is called: (Gerontology, Ecology,
Genecology: None of above)
Explanation:
The correct term for the study of ancestors, family
history, and tracing their lineage is Genealogy. It involves
investigating family records, historical documents, and
genetic data to construct family trees and understand
heritage.
Gerontology refers to the study of aging and the elderly.
Ecology is the study of the relationships between living
organisms and their environment.
Genecology is the study of genetic variation within
species in relation to their ecological environment.
Since none of the given options correspond to
Genealogy, the correct answer is (D) None of the above.
64. Light of the sun can be focused on the following
lens: (Convex)
Associated Information:
Here are the basic types of lenses with their
characteristics and uses, including their roles in
correcting vision:
Convex Lens: Converges light rays, making objects
appear larger and closer.
o Uses: Magnifying glasses, Cameras, Telescopes,
Binoculars, Microscopes, Laser beam focusing,
Correcting farsightedness (hyperopia)
Concave Lens: Diverges light rays, making objects appear
smaller and farther away.
o Uses: Corrective lenses for nearsightedness
(myopia), Peepholes, Laser beam expansion,
Optical instruments (e.g., telescopes, microscopes),
Virtual reality headsets
Note: Convex lenses are used to correct farsightedness
(hyperopia) because they converge light rays, enabling
close objects to be seen clearly. Concave lenses are used
to correct nearsightedness (myopia) because they
diverge light rays, allowing distant objects to be seen
clearly.
Explanation: A convex lens focuses the light of the sun
because it converges the light rays to a point. This
property is why convex lenses are used for tasks like
magnification and laser beam focusing.

80. WOW! is an: (Interjection)
Associated Information:
In English grammar, parts of speech are categories that
classify words based on their functions in a sentence.
Traditionally, there are eight parts of speech, but some
frameworks include a ninth category for articles or
determiners. Below is a detailed breakdown:
1. Nouns (N): Words that name persons, places,
things, or ideas.
o Examples: "book," "city," "happiness"
o Types: Proper nouns (e.g., "London"), common
nouns (e.g., "city"), countable nouns (e.g., "apple"),
uncountable nouns (e.g., "water").
2. Pronouns (PN): Words that replace nouns to avoid
repetition.
o Examples: "he," "she," "it," "they"
o Types: Personal pronouns (e.g., "I"), possessive
pronouns (e.g., "mine"), demonstrative pronouns
(e.g., "this"), interrogative pronouns (e.g., "who").
3. Verbs (V): Words that express actions, states, or
occurrences.
o Examples: "run," "write," "be," "have"
o Types: Action verbs (e.g., "jump"), linking verbs
(e.g., "is"), helping verbs (e.g., "can").
4. Adjectives (ADJ): Words that describe or modify
nouns or pronouns.
o Examples: "happy," "big," "blue," "cold"
o Types: Descriptive (e.g., "red"), quantitative (e.g.,
"many"), comparative (e.g., "better"), superlative
(e.g., "best").


--- Page 103 ---
5. Adverbs (ADV): Words that modify verbs,
adjectives, or other adverbs, answering "how,"
"when," "where," or "to what extent."
Examples: "quickly," "very," "well," "yesterday"
Types: Manner (e.g., "gracefully"), time (e.g.,
"later"), place (e.g., "here"), degree (e.g., "almost").
6. Prepositions (P): Words that show relationships
between nouns (or pronouns) and other words in a
sentence.
Examples: "in," "on," "with," "under"
7. Conjunctions (CONJ): Words that connect words,
phrases, or clauses.
Examples: "and," "but," "because," "or"
Types: Coordinating (e.g., "and"), subordinating
(e.g., "although"), correlative (e.g., "either/or").
8. Interjections (INT): Words that express emotions,
reactions, or feelings, often standing alone.
Examples: "wow," "ouch," "ah," "hooray"
Additional Category:
9. Articles or Determiners (A/D): Some frameworks
consider articles ("the," "a," "an") or determiners ("this,"
"that," "some") as a distinct part of speech, though
traditionally grouped under adjectives.
Modern Grammar Perspective: While the traditional
system of eight parts of speech is widely taught, modern
linguists recognize additional categories like particles
(e.g., "up" in "give up") or modal verbs (e.g., "can,"
"might").

4. "Petronas Towers" is located in: (Kuala
Lumpur)
Associated Information:
The Petronas Towers, also known as the Petronas Twin
Towers, are iconic skyscrapers in Kuala Lumpur,
Malaysia.
Key Facts:
Height: 452 meters (1,483 feet)
Floors: 88
Completed: 1998
Architect: César Pelli
Engineer: Thornton Tomasetti
Purpose: Office spaces, observation decks, and a
shopping mall
When completed in 1998, the Petronas Towers were the
tallest buildings in the world until 2004. They were
surpassed by Taipei 101 in Taiwan, which held the title
until 2010.
Timeline of the World's Tallest Buildings:
1. Petronas Towers (1998-2004): 452 meters
2. Taipei 101 (2004-2010): 508 meters
3. Burj Khalifa (2010-present): 828 meters
The Burj Khalifa, located in Dubai, UAE, is currently the
tallest building in the world.
The Petronas Towers remain a symbol of Malaysia's
modern development and a popular tourist attraction.

12. "Sense and Sensibility" was written by: (Jane
Austin)
Associated Information:
Jane Austen (1775-1817) was a celebrated English
novelist known for her timeless works of romantic
fiction. Her novels focus on themes of love, society, and
personal growth, often critiquing the societal norms of
her time.
Key Works by Jane Austen:
1. Sense and Sensibility (1811)
2. Pride and Prejudice (1813)
3. Mansfield Park (1814)
4. Emma (1816)
5. Northanger Abbey (1818, published posthumously)
6. Persuasion (1818, published posthumously)
7. Lady Susan (1871, published posthumously)
Interesting Facts:
* Born in Steventon, Hampshire, England, she was
the seventh of eight children.
* She never married, dedicating her life to her
writing.
* She originally published her novels anonymously
under the pseudonym "A Lady."
* Despite her remarkable talent, she lived modestly
and struggled with poor health.
* She passed away at the young age of 41 in 1817.
Jane Austen's novels remain beloved classics, admired
for their wit, insight, and social commentary. "Sense and
Sensibility" was her first published novel, marking the
beginning of her literary legacy.

16. The idea of Liberty, Equality and Fraternity was
given by: (Rousseau)
Associated Information:
Jean-Jacques Rousseau (1712-1778), a key figure of the
Enlightenment, popularized the concept of "Liberty,
Equality, and Fraternity" in his book "The Social
Contract" (1762). His ideas influenced the French
Revolution and modern political thought, emphasizing
individual freedom, equality, and collective governance
through the "general will."
About the Enlightenment:
The Enlightenment (17th-18th Century), or Age of
Reason, emphasized reason, individual rights, and
secular governance. Thinkers like Rousseau, Locke,
Montesquieu, and Voltaire advocated for freedom,
equality, and scientific progress, challenging traditional
authority.
About the French Revolution (1789-1799):
Influenced by Enlightenment ideas, the French
Revolution sought to overthrow monarchy and
feudalism. It popularized Liberty, Equality, and
Fraternity as guiding principles, leading to:
Key Events: Storming of the Bastille, abolition of feudal
privileges, and the Rights of Man declaration.
Impact: Inspired global democratic movements and
strengthened ideals of secularism, citizenship, and
human rights.
Philosophical Contributions:
Rousseau: Liberty, equality, and governance by the
general will.
Hobbes: Strong government for order.
Montesquieu: Separation of powers.
Locke: Natural rights (life, liberty, property).
The Enlightenment, French Revolution, and Rousseau's
ideas shaped the foundation of modern democracy and
human rights.
17. "Malabar" was the ancient name of: (Madras)
18. "First Technology" of man on the earth is: (Use
of Fire)
Explanation:
The use of fire is considered the first technology of early
humans. It marked a turning point in human evolution,
allowing them to cook food, stay warm, protect
themselves from predators, and expand to colder
regions. This technological breakthrough is believed to
have occurred approximately 1.5 million years ago,
during the Lower Paleolithic period. Other technologies,
like the use of tools, cloth, and paper, came much later
in human history.

27. The United Nations was founded on: (October

Associated Information:
The United Nations (UN) was established on October 24,
1945, following the end of World War II, to promote
peace, security, and international cooperation. It
replaced the League of Nations and remains the most
influential global organization.
Key Founding Figures:
1. Cordell Hull (American)
* Known as the "Father of the United Nations."
* U.S. Secretary of State (1933-1944).
* Played a pivotal role in planning the UN during
WWII.
* Awarded the Nobel Peace Prize (1945) for his
efforts.

--- Page 105 ---
2. Franklin D. Roosevelt (American)
* Coined the term "United Nations" in 1942.
* Initiated the drafting of the UN Charter and
provided strong leadership.
3. Winston Churchill (British)
* Advocated for a new International body and co-
signed the Atlantic Charter.
4. Joseph Stalin (Soviet)
* Played a key role in designing the UN's structure
and veto system.
5. Harry Truman (American)
* Signed the UN Charter at the San Francisco
Conference (June 1945).
6. Trygve Lie (Norwegian)
* First Secretary-General of the UN.
7. Eleanor Roosevelt (American)
* Chaired the UN Commission on Human Rights and
helped draft the Universal Declaration of Human
Rights.
Additional Contributors:
* Jan Smuts (South African): Helped draft the UN
Charter.
* Carlos Romulo (Filipino): Advocated for the UN's
development agenda.
* Lester B. Pearson (Canadian): Contributed to
peacekeeping functions.
* Peter Fraser (New Zealander): Played a role in
drafting the Charter.
* Anthony Eden (British), Vyacheslav Molotov
(Soviet), and others were instrumental in shaping
the UN's early structure.
The United Nations Charter was signed on June 26,
1945, by 50 nations, and the organization officially came
into existence on October 24, 1945, now celebrated
annually as United Nations Day.

30. Common Man's Gallery is inaugurated on 4th

31. The Indus Valley Civilization belongs to:
(Chalcolithic age)
Associated Information:
The Indus Valley Civilization (IVC) belonged to the
Chalcolithic age, also known as the Bronze Age. This
period marked a transition from the Neolithic age (stone
tools) to the Iron Age (iron tools). The IVC is renowned
for its advanced urban planning, use of bronze tools, and
sophisticated irrigation systems.
Overview of Historical Ages:
Paleolithic age (Old Stone Age): Early humans used
stone tools and lived as hunter-gatherers. (Approx. 2.5
million - 10,000 BCE)
Mesolithic age (Middle Stone Age): Marked by the use
of microliths (small stone tools) and the rise of early
settlements. (Approx. 10,000-5,000 BCE)

Papers of 2019
105
Neolithic age (New Stone Age): Era of agriculture,
animal domestication, and permanent villages. (Approx.
5,000-2,000 BCE)
Chalcolithic age (Copper-Stone Age): Transition to metal
tools, especially copper and bronze. (Approx. 2,000 -
1,500 BCE)
Iron Age: Widespread use of iron tools and weapons.
(Approx. 1,500 BCE - 500 CE)
The Indus Valley Civilization, flourishing between 3300
and 1300 BCE, is a prime example of the Chalcolithic age
and showcases early advancements in technology, trade,
and governance.

51. Milk contains water (80%)

--- Page 106 ---
106 Advanced PPSC MCQs Papers (Volume 2)
Explanation:
The question asks about the water content in milk, and
we calculated the average water content for common
types of milk (cow, buffalo, and goat). The result was
approximately 85%.
Now, comparing the given options (70%, 75%, 80%,
90%), both 80% and 90% are 5% away from 85%, making
them equidistant. This raises the question: Should we
round down to 80% or up to 90%?
Why 80% is More Justifiable than 90%?
1. Closer to Buffalo Milk: Buffalo milk, which has the
lowest water content (~81-83%), pulls the average
down. Since no common milk naturally reaches
90%, choosing 80% is a safer approximation.
2. Scientific Estimates Favor ~87%: Cow's milk is the
most commonly referenced standard for general
milk composition, and it contains ~87% water,
which is closer to 80% than 90%.
3. Avoiding Overestimation: If we choose 90%, we
might imply that milk contains more water than it
actually does, whereas 80% is still within a
reasonable range.
Final Conclusion:
* Exact average: 85%
* Best approximation from given options: 80% (since
rounding up to 90% would be an overestimation).
* Thus, 80% is the most justifiable answer based on
available choices.

Basic Mathematics
59. Complete the series: 2, 4, 3, 9, 4, 16, 5, 25, 6......
(36)
Solution:
2, 4, 3, 9, 4, 16, 5, 25, 6, 36
2² 3² 4² 5² 6²
2² = 4, 3² = 9
4² = 16, 5² = 25
6² = 36
60. If 15 toys cost Rs.234, what do 35 toys cost:
(Rs.546)
Solution:
15 toys cost = 234
1 toys cost = 234 / 15
= 15.6
35 toys cost = 35 x 15.6
= 546
61. Complete: 10,20,40,80, _________ (160)
Solution:
10, 20, 40, 80, 160
x2 x2 x2 x2
10 x 2 = 20
20 x 2 = 40
40 x 2 = 80
80 x 2 = 160
62. Evaluate: 2x25+5+10-2 (18)
Solution:
2x25+5+10-2
= 2x 5+10-2
= 10+10-2
= 20-2
= 18
63. Evaluate: 0.213÷0.00213 (100)
Solution:
0.213÷0.00213
= 213/1000 ÷ 213/100000
= 213/1000 x 100000/213
= 100000/1000
= 100
64. Which one of the number completes the series.
2, 5, 8, 11, 14... (17)

+3 +3 +3 +3 +3

--- Page 107 ---
2 + 3 = 5,
8+3 = 11,
14+3=17
5+3=8
11+3=14
65. Find the mean proportion between 5 and 45.
(15)
Solution:
Mean proportion
5 : x :: x : 45
x² = 5 x 45
x² = 225
x = √225
x = 15
66. The ratio of two numbers a and b is 3:5. If 2 is
added to both the numbers, the ratio becomes
2:3. Find b? (10)
Solution:
a : b = 3 : 5
a/b = 3/5
5a = 3b
a = 3b/5
If 2 is added then
(a+2)/(b+2) = 2/3
3(a+2) = 2(b+2)
3a+6 = 2b+4
3(3b/5)+6 = 2b+4
9b/5 + 6 = 2b+4
9b/5 = 2b+4-6
9b/5 = 2b-2
9b = 5(2b-2)
9b = 10b-10
10b-9b = 10
b = 10
67. A bag contains 50 paise, 1 rupee and 2 rupee
coins in the ratio 2:5:8. If the total amount is Rs.
352, find the total number of coins in the bag.
(240)
Solution:
Let the number be 2x, 5x and 8x.
0.5 x 2x + 1 x 5x + 2 x 8x = 352
x + 5x + 16x = 352
22x = 352
x = 352/22
x = 16
Total number of coins = 2x + 5x + 8x
= 15x
= 15 x 16 = 240

Occupation: Novelist, philosopher, social reformer
Famous Works:
1. War and Peace (1869) - An epic novel about
Russian society during the Napoleonic Wars.
2. Anna Karenina (1877) - A tragic love story exploring
moral and societal themes.
3. The Death of Ivan Ilyich (1886) - A novella

• Advocated for non-violence, simplicity, and
spirituality.

Martin Luther King Jr. with his ideas on pacifism and
civil disobedience.
Legacy:
Tolstoy is regarded as one of the greatest novelists in
history, renowned for his profound storytelling and
exploration of human nature, morality, and social issues.
His works remain central to world literature and
philosophy.

Associated Information:
Original Seven Wonders of the Ancient World:
Compiled by Antipater of Sidon around 140 BCE, the list
celebrated remarkable architectural and artistic
achievements of the ancient world:
1. The Great Pyramid of Giza (Egypt):
Ο The only surviving wonder from the original list.
Ο Built around 2550 BCE as a tomb for Pharaoh Khufu.
2. The Hanging Gardens of Babylon (Iraq):
Ο Believed to have been built by King
Nebuchadnezzar II.
Ο Its exact location remains a mystery.
3. The Statue of Zeus at Olympia (Greece):
Ο A massive gold and ivory statue, destroyed in a fire
in the 5th century CE.
4. The Temple of Artemis at Ephesus (Türkiye):
Ο A grand temple dedicated to Artemis, destroyed by
arson in 356 BCE.
5. The Mausoleum at Halicarnassus (Türkiye):
Ο A tomb combining Greek, Egyptian, and Lycian
styles.
6. The Colossus of Rhodes (Greece):
Ο A gigantic bronze statue toppled by an earthquake
in 226 BCE.
7. The Lighthouse of Alexandria (Egypt):
Ο Built on Pharos Island to guide sailors into
Alexandria's port.
Ο One of the tallest structures of its time (over 100
meters).
Ο Destroyed by earthquakes in the 14th century.
New Seven Wonders of the World (2007):
Selected via a global poll in 2007, these monuments
reflect humanity's architectural brilliance across ages:
1. The Great Wall of China (China): Symbol of
resilience, spanning over 13,000 miles.
2. The Taj Mahal (India): A marble masterpiece built
in memory of Mumtaz Mahal.
3. Machu Picchu (Peru): Incan citadel hidden in the
Andes.

--- Page 109 ---
Papers of 2019 109
4. Chichén Itzá (Mexico): Famous for the El Castillo
pyramid and Mayan astronomy.
5. The Roman Colosseum (Italy): An Iconic
amphitheater symbolizing Roman engineering.
6. Christ the Redeemer (Brazil): A symbol of peace
overlooking Rio de Janeiro.
7. The Great Pyramid of Giza (Egypt): Included as an
honorary wonder, as it features in both the ancient
and modern lists.
Key Facts About the Lighthouse of Alexandria:
• Built around 280 BCE during the reign of Ptolemy II.
• Stood on Pharos Island and guided ships into
Alexandria's port.
• Its height and design made it a technological marvel
of its time.
• Destroyed by earthquakes in the 14th century.
The Lighthouse of Alexandria symbolizes ancient
innovation and maritime importance, a timeless legacy
of human ingenuity.

90. Which of the following is divisible by 2, 3 and 5?
(390)
Solution:
Let's break down the solution step by step:
1. We need to find a number that is divisible by 2, 3, and
5.

--- Page 111 ---
Papers of 2019 111
2. To be divisible by 2, the number must be even (end in
0, 2, 4, 6, or 8).
3. To be divisible by 3, the sum of the digits must be a
multiple of 3 (e.g., 3, 6, 9, 12, ...).
4. To be divisible by 5, the number must end In 0 or 5.
Now, let's analyze 390:
• Even, so divisible by 2.
• Sum of digits: 3+9+0 = 12, which is a multiple of 3, so
divisible by 3.
• Ends in 0, so divisible by 5.

92. If 3/11 of a number is 22, what is 6/11 of that
number? (48)
Solution:
We need to determine the value of 6/11 of a number
given that 3/11 of the number is equal to 22.
Step 1: Let the unknown number be "x". The given
information can be represented as:
3/11 * x = 22
Step 2: To solve for "x", multiply both sides by the
reciprocal of 3/11:
x = 22* (11/3)
x = (22*11)/3,
x = 88
Thus, the value of the number is 88.
Step 3: Find 6/11 of the number:
6/11 * 88 = (6 * 88) / 11 = 48
Final Answer:
The value of 6/11 of the number is:
(D) 48

55. The first session of All India Muslim League
was held at: (Karachi)
Associated Information:
The event on December 30, 1906, held in Dhaka (Dacca),
was the annual session of the All-India Muhammadan
Educational Conference. During this session, the
decision to establish the All-India Muslim League (AIML)
as a political party was made. This event was presided
over by Nawab Sir Salimullah of Dhaka, who was a key
advocate for the creation of the Muslim League.
The first regular session of the AIML was held later in
Karachi in December 1907. This session marked the
formal operational beginning of the Muslim League,
during which key resolutions were passed to outline the
party's objectives and strategies. This session was
presided over by Adamjee Peerbhoy, a prominent
businessman and an early supporter of the AIML.

58. Total number of round table conference held in
London? (3)
Associated Information:
The Round Table Conferences were a series of peace
conferences organized by the British Government
between 1930 and 1932. Their objective was to discuss
constitutional reforms in India and chart a path toward
self-governance.
First Round Table Conference (November 1930 –
January 1931):
* Venue: House of Commons, London, UK
* Context: Emerged from the review of the
  Government of India Act, 1919, conducted by the
  Simon Commission in 1927.
* Key Participants:
  * British Representatives: Prime Minister Ramsay
    MacDonald, Secretary of State William Wedgwood
    Benn, and others (16 participants).
  * Indian National Congress: Absent, as it was
    engaged in a civil disobedience campaign (0
    participants).
  * Muslim League: Muhammad Ali Jinnah, Allama
    Iqbal, and others (15 participants).
  * Other Participants: Sir Muhammad Zafarullah
    Khan, Allama Iqbal, and others (10 participants).
* Total Participants: 41.
* Outcome:
  * Emphasized the federal principle and the need for
    a parliamentary system.
  * All participants, including princely state
    representatives, accepted the goal of dominion
    status for India.
* Muslim League's Role:
  * Jinnah proposed the "Fourteen Points"
    advocating Muslim representation and
    protection of rights.
  * Allama Iqbal stressed the need for a separate
    homeland for Muslims.
Second Round Table Conference (September –
December 1931):
* Venue: House of Commons, London, UK
* Context: Built on the first conference to address
  communal representation and constitutional
  reforms.
* Key Participants:
  * British Representatives: Same as the first
    conference (16 participants).
  * Indian National Congress: Represented by
    Mahatma Gandhi, alongside Jawaharlal Nehru, Sir
    Tej Bahadur Sapru, and others (20 participants).
  * Women Representatives:
    * Sarojini Naidu (Indian National Congress).
    * Begum Shah Nawaz and Shareefa Hamid Ali
      (Muslim League) (2 participants).
  * Muslim League: Jinnah, Allama Iqbal, and others
    advocated for Muslim rights (15 participants).
* Total Participants: 53.
* Outcome:
  * No consensus was reached on constitutional
    reforms or communal representation.
  * Highlighted divisions within the Indian nationalist
    movement.
  * Muslim League's Role: Insisted on separate
    electorates for Muslims.
  * Allama Iqbal's Contribution: Reiterated the
    necessity of a separate homeland for Muslims.
Third Round Table Conference (November - December
1932):
* Venue: House of Commons, London, UK
* Context: Aimed to finalize constitutional reforms,
  focusing on federalism and provincial autonomy.
* Key Participants:
  * British Representatives: Prime Minister Ramsay
    MacDonald and Secretary of State Sir Samuel Hoare
    (2 participants).
  * Indian Representatives: Muhammad Ali Jinnah, Sir
    Muhammad Zafarullah Khan, and others (15
    participants).
* Total Participants: 32.
* Note: Allama Iqbal did not attend this conference.
* Outcome:
  * Lacked progress due to limited representation, as
    the Indian National Congress boycotted the
    conference.
Historical Significance:
* The Round Table Conferences provided a platform
  for dialogue between British officials and Indian
  leaders but exposed significant divisions among
  Indian political groups.

--- Page 114 ---
* While they didn't fully achieve their goals, they laid
  the groundwork for the Government of India Act,
  1935, which introduced provincial autonomy and
  proposed a federal system (never fully
  implemented).
* These conferences marked an important step in
  India's constitutional history and journey toward
  self-governance.
* Allama Iqbal's contributions during the first two
  conferences emphasized the importance of Muslim
  representation and the demand for a separate
  homeland for Muslims, which later became the
  foundation for the creation of Pakistan.

67 The Wakhan corridor separates Pakistan from:
  (Tajikistan)
Associated Information:
Pakistan's Borders and Geography:
Pakistan shares a 1,046-kilometer (650-mile) coastline
along the Arabian Sea and is bordered by:
* India to the east
* Afghanistan to the west
* Iran to the southwest
* China to the northeast
Additionally, Pakistan is narrowly separated from
Tajikistan by the Wakhan Corridor, a narrow strip of
land in northeastern Afghanistan.
The Wakhan Corridor:
A 350 km (220 mi) long and 13 to 65 km (8 to 40 mi) wide
strip in northeastern Afghanistan.
Connects Afghanistan to China's Xinjiang region.
Geographical Significance:
* Separates Tajikistan from Pakistan and Kashmir.
* Lies between the Pamir Mountains in the north and
  the Karakoram Range in the south.
Rivers: The Panj and Pamir Rivers emerge here, forming
the Amu Darya River.
Historical Context:
The Wakhan Corridor was established in the 19th
Durand Line Agreement between the British Raj and
Afghanistan. It served as a buffer zone between the
Russian Empire (now Tajikistan) and the British Empire
(now Pakistan).
Key Features of the Corridor:
* Forms a rugged and remote region with limited
  access.
* Historically used as a trade route between Central
  Asia, South Asia, and East Asia.
* Acts as a strategic location due to its proximity to
  Afghanistan, Pakistan, China, and Tajikistan.
The Wakhan Corridor remains geopolitically significant,
creating a natural separation between Pakistan and
Tajikistan while linking Afghanistan with China.

79 Sphygmomanometer is an instrument used to
  measure ________ (Blood Pressure)
Associated Information:
Diagnostic Instruments:
Stethoscope: Used to listen to internal body sounds
such as the heartbeat, lung sounds, and bowel
movements. (Helps detect abnormalities like murmurs,
arrhythmias, or respiratory issues)
Thermometer: Measures body temperature. (Helps
identify fever, hypothermia, or infections)
Sphygmomanometer: Measures blood pressure. (Helps
diagnose hypertension, hypotension, or cardiovascular
conditions)
Otoscope: Used to examine the ear canal and eardrum.
(Detects ear infections, blockages, or perforations in the
eardrum)
Ophthalmoscope: Used to examine the interior of the
eye, including the retina and optic nerve. (Helps
diagnose conditions like glaucoma, diabetic retinopathy,
or retinal detachment)
Pulse Oximeter: Measures oxygen saturation levels in
the blood and pulse rate. (Monitors respiratory or
cardiac issues, such as hypoxemia or pneumonia)

--- Page 115 ---
Electrocardiogram (ECG or EKG) Machine: Records the
electrical activity of the heart. (Diagnoses arrhythmias,
heart attacks, or other cardiac abnormalities)
Endoscope: A flexible or rigid tube with a camera used
to view internal organs or cavities. (Identifies conditions
like ulcers, tumors, or blockages in the gastrointestinal
tract)
Ultrasound Machine: Uses sound waves to create
images of internal organs and tissues. (Monitors
pregnancies, detects organ abnormalities, or guides
biopsies)
MRI (Magnetic Resonance Imaging) Scanner: Uses
magnetic fields and radio waves to produce detailed
images of soft tissues. (Diagnoses brain tumors, joint
problems, or spinal cord injuries)
X-Ray Machine: Uses radiation to produce images of
bones and certain tissues. (Detects fractures, infections,
or lung conditions like pneumonia)
CT (Computed Tomography) Scanner: Creates cross-
sectional images of the body using X-rays. (Diagnoses
cancers, internal injuries, or blood clots)
Mammography Machine: Specialized X-ray for breast
imaging. (Detects early signs of breast cancer or other
abnormalities)
Glucometer: Measures blood glucose levels. (Monitors
diabetes and helps manage blood sugar levels)
Laryngoscope: Used to view the larynx and vocal cords.
(Commonly used during intubation or to diagnose throat
conditions)
Colposcope: Magnifies and illuminates the cervix and
vagina for examination. (Detects cervical abnormalities
and guides biopsies)
Tuning Fork: Produces vibrations to assess hearing or
detect nerve damage. (Used in hearing tests or to
diagnose fractures)
Spirometer: Measures lung capacity and airflow.
(Diagnoses conditions like asthma or COPD)
Dermatoscope: Magnifies the skin for detailed
examination. (Identifies skin lesions, moles, and early
signs of skin cancer)

Associated Information:
"Politics Among Nations: The Struggle for Power and

--- Page 116 ---
Peace" is a foundational book in the field of international
relations, written by Hans J. Morgenthau. First
published in 1948, it is considered a seminal work in the
realist school of thought. The book emphasizes the
concept of power as the central element in politics and
international relations, introducing the principles of
political realism, which argue that international politics
is governed by objective laws rooted in human nature. It
has been widely influential in shaping both academic
discourse and practical foreign policy strategies.

Pakistan Studies
20. Who presented the Poor man Budget of United
  India Interim Government? (Liaqat Ali Khan)
Associated Information:
Interim Government of India: The Interim Government
of India was formed on 2nd September 1946, as a
transitional arrangement before India's independence. It
was headed by Jawaharlal Nehru as the Vice President
of the Executive Council (effectively the Prime Minister).
Composition: The government included members from
the Indian National Congress, the Muslim League, and
other groups.
Role of Liaqat Ali Khan: Liaqat Ali Khan, as the finance
minister, presented the "Poor Man's Budget" in 1947,
aimed at reducing economic disparities by introducing
heavy taxation on the rich and providing relief to the
poor.
Significance: This government played a key role in
framing policies that paved the way for India's
independence in 1947.

60. What is 11 in binary? (1011)
Solution:
2 | 11
2 | 5 - 1
2 | 2 - 1
1 | 0
  = (1011)
61. 40 x 5.9 = ________ (236)
Solution:
  40 x 59
  = 236
62. In a group of 550 students 42% go to a tour.
  How many students go to the tour? (231)
Solution:
  Total students = 550
  42% go to tour
  = 42/100 × 550
  = 4.2 x 55
  = 231
63. Simplify: (8(11-2) - 5(11-2))/3 = ? (9)
Solution:
  (8(11-2) - 5(11-2)) / 3 = ?
  (8(9) - 5(9)) / 3
  (72 - 45) / 3
  27 / 3
  = 9
64. What will be the Least Common Multiple of 5,
  15, 20 and 25? (300).
Solution:
  Least common multiple 5, 15, 20 and 25
  5 | 5, 15, 20, 25
  3 | 1, 3, 4, 5
  4 | 1, 1, 4, 5
  5 | 1, 1, 1, 5
  | 1, 1, 1, 1
  5 x 3 x 4 x 5 = 300
  L.C.M = 300
65. Find the odd one out, 8, 27, 64, 100, 125. 215.
  343 (100)
Solution:
  8, 27, 64, 100, 125, 216, 343
  The pattern is
  2³, 3³, 4³, 5³, 6³, 7³
  But 100 is not a perfect cube.
66. If 15:7:: x: 560 then x = (1200)
Solution:
  15 : 7 :: x : 560
  15/7 = x/560
  x = (15 * 560) / 7
  x = 15 * 80
  x = 1200
67. A bookseller sold a book for Rs. 40.00 to make
  a profit of 15% percent. In order to earn a profit
  of 20%, he should have sold it for. (41.74)
Solution:
  Selling Price (SP) = Rs. 40
  Profit % = 15%
  CP = SP / (1 + Profit %)
  = 40 / (1 + 0.15)
  = 40 / 1.15
  = Rs. 34.78
  Now, to find the new selling price for a 20%
  profit:
  New SP = CP + (20% of CP)
  = 34.78 + (0.20 x 34.78)
  = 34.78 + 6.96
  = Rs. 41.74
  The correct answer is: (A) 41.74
68. If A is two years older than B and B is twice as
  old as C. If the sum of the ages of A, B and C Is
  27 then how old is B? (10)
Solution:
  Let C age = x year
  B age = 2x
  A age = (2x + 2)
  Sum of the ages of A, B and C is 27.
  x + 2x + (2x + 2) = 27
  5x + 2 = 27
  5x = 27 - 2
  5x = 25
  x = 25 / 5
  x = 5

18. Immanuel Kant was a
Philosopher.
(A) French
(B) British:
(C) Polish
(D) German
Associated Information:
Full Name: Immanuel Kant (1724-1804).
Nationality: German.
Key Works: "Critique of Pure Reason," "Critique of
Practical Reason," and "Critique of Judgment."
Philosophical Contributions:
Epistemology: Proposed the "Copernican Revolution" in
philosophy, emphasizing that our perception shapes
reality.
Ethics: Developed the Categorical Imperative, focusing
on universal moral laws and duty-based ethics.
•
•
Metaphysics: Distinguished between phenomena
(what we perceive) and noumena (things-in-
themselves).
Aesthetics: Explored beauty and the sublime,
suggesting aesthetic judgment is both subjective
and universal.
Legacy: Influenced modern philosophy, including
German Idealism, existentialism, and analytic
philosophy.

51. One of the following is not a function of bones
in human body? (Secretion of hormones)
Associated Information:
Bones do not secrete hormones. However, bones do
have a role in regulating mineral homeostasis, such as
calcium and phosphorus, which is crucial for various
bodily functions.
The other options are all functions of bones in the
human body:
(A) Protection of vital organs: Bones provide a protective
framework for internal organs, such as the skull
protecting the brain and the rib cage protecting the
heart and lungs.
(C) Place for muscle attachment: Bones serve as
attachment points for muscles, allowing for movement
and mobility.
(D) Production of blood corpuscles: The bone marrow
within certain bones, such as the pelvis and femur, is
responsible for producing blood cells, including red and
white blood cells and platelets.
So, the correct answer is (B) Secretion of hormones.

Bulk Modulus (KKK) is a measure of a material's
resistance to uniform compression. It is defined as the
ratio of the change in pressure to the relative change in
volume.

prime.
(2,4)

ضرب المثل کی تعریف
جو علامت استعمال ہوتی ہے وہ کہلاتی ہے۔ (فجائیہ)
رموز اوقاف
تعریف : رموز اوقاف اردو تحریر میں جملے کے اندر اور اختتام پر ٹھہر آؤ، وضاحت، یا معنی کی
ضرب المثل ایسے مختصر اور جامع جملے یا اقوال کو کہتے ہیں جو کسی خاص حقیقت یا تجربے کو موثر درستگی کے لیے استعمال ہونے والے نشانات ہیں۔ یہ جملے کے مفہوم کو واضح اور مؤثر بناتے
ہیں۔
اور عام فہم انداز میں بیان کریں۔ یہ جملے اکثر طویل گفتگو کا خلاصہ کرتے ہیں اور اپنی
جامعیت اور معنویت کی وجہ سے مقبول ہوتے ہیں۔ ضرب الامثال زندگی کے مختلف پہلوؤں اہم رموز اوقاف اور ان کے اردو نام:
کی عکاسی کرتے ہیں اور ان میں حکمت ، نصیحت، یا طنز پوشیدہ ہوتا ہے۔
ضرب المثل کی خصوصیات:
ثالیں:
1
جامعیت : مختصر اور پر اثر ہوتے ہیں۔
2 حکمت و نصیحت : عملی زندگی کے تجربات پر مبنی ہوتے ہیں۔
معروف و مقبول : عوام میں عام طور پر مشہور اور قابل فہم ہوتے ہیں۔

محاورہ کی تعریف
محاورہ مخصوص الفاظ یا جملوں کے ایسے مجموعے کو کہتے ہیں جو اپنے ظاہری معنی کے بجائے
مجازی یا مخصوص معنوں میں استعمال ہوتا ہے ۔ محاورہ گفتگو میں روانی، خوبصورتی، اور اظہار
کے رنگ بھرنے کے لیے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے۔
محاورے کی خصوصیات:
1. مخصوص معنی : الفاظ کے مجموعے کا مطلب اکثر انفرادی الفاظ کے معنی سے
مختلف ہوتا ہے۔
2. روانی اور دلکشی : تفنگو یا تحریر کو پرکشش اور دلنشین بناتا ہے۔
3. ثقافتی رنگ : محاورے کسی قوم کی ثقافت، روایات، اور طرز زندگی کی عکاسی
کرتے ہیں۔
4. استعمال کا مقصد : کسی بات کو مجازی، طنزیہ یا دلچسپ انداز میں بیان کرنا۔
مثالیں:
• کھسیانی بلی کھمبا نوچے۔
• آسمان سے گرا، کھجور میں اٹکا۔
• دم دبا کر بھاگنا۔
ضرب المثل اور محاورہ میں فرق:
| پہلو | محاورہ | ضرب المثل |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| تعریف | مخصوص الفاظ کا مجموعہ جو مجازی معنوں میں استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ | مختصر جملے جو نصیحت یا سبق دیتے ہیں۔ |
| معنی | اکثر مجازی یا علامتی ہوتے ہیں۔ | عام طور پر واضح اور نصیحت آموز ہوتے ہیں۔ |
| استعمال | گفتگو کو دلچسپ اور رواں بنانے کے لیے۔ | گفتگو کو سبق آموز اور پر اثر بنانے کے لیے۔ |
| خود مختاری | محاورہ مکمل جملہ نہیں بلکہ جملے کا حصہ ہوتا ہے۔ | ضرب المثل مکمل جملہ ہوتا ہے۔ |
| مثال | جلتی پر تیل ڈالنا۔ | نیکی کر، دریا میں ڈال۔ |

اختتامیہ
ضرب المثل اور محاورہ دونوں زبان کی خوبصورتی، روانی، اور مؤثریت کو بڑھاتے ہیں۔ ضرب
الامثال نصیحت، حکمت، اور زندگی کے تجربات کا نچوڑ پیش کرتے ہیں، جبکہ محاورے گفتگو کو
دلکش اور دلچسپ بناتے ہیں۔ اردو زبان میں ان دونوں کا استعمال ادب اور روز مرہ زندگی کا
ایک اہم حصہ ہے، جو تحریر اور گفتگو کو اثر انگیز اور معنی خیز بناتا ہے۔

General Knowledge
1. Iraq occupied Kuwait in: (August 1990)
Associated Information:
Kuwait's Historical Background
1. Formation of Kuwait as a City:
    * Kuwait was established in the 18th century by the
      Bani Utub tribe.
    * Initially, it was a small mud-walled settlement
      reliant on fishing, pearling, and trade.
2. Ottoman Rule (1871-1899):
    * From 1871 to 1899, Kuwait was under the Ottoman
      Empire, administered as part of the Basra Vilayet
      (province).
    * Despite Ottoman control, Kuwait maintained some
      degree of local autonomy under the Al-Sabah
      dynasty.
3. British Protectorate and Independence:
    * To avoid Ottoman domination, Kuwait became a
      British protectorate in 1899 under an agreement
      that ensured British military protection In exchange
      for control over foreign policy.
    * Kuwait gained full independence on June 19, 1961,
      formally ending the British protectorate.
4. Separation from Iraq and Modern Era:
    * In 1932, Kuwait was formally recognized as a
      separate entity, distinct from Iraq.
    * In August 1990, Iraq invaded Kuwait, claiming
      historical ties and disputes over oil fields. This
      invasion triggered the Gulf War.
    * Kuwait was liberated in 1991 by an international
      coalition led by the United States, marking the end
      of the Iraqi occupation.
